International Commercial Telegraph

-Reuters Special Commercial Report on May 3rd- Gold and Silver 92

London Gold Price: Today (May 3rd), the London gold price is 136 shillings, down 3.5 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Bar: Today (May 3rd), the London silver market is very quiet. The spot price is quoted at 18.75 pence, up 0.0625. The futures price is 18.8125 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price. China sold and India bought on this day, and the market closed steadily.

New York Silver Bar: Today (May 3rd), the silver market initially trended steady due to the London telegraph and rumors of a new silver faction movement in Washington. Later, it turned quiet, waiting for new news from Washington. Public belief is that the power to control the situation is still in the hands of President Roosevelt. The opening price of forward silver is 0.50 to 0.91 pounds higher than yesterday's closing price.

Bombay Silver Bar: Today (May 3rd), the Bombay silver market is quiet and stable. The spot price is 51 rupees and 10 annas, the same as yesterday's price. The prices for May-June are also unchanged.

Exchange Rates 93

British-American: Today (May 3rd), the London foreign exchange market is very quiet. The British-American exchange rate opened at $5.1225, the same as yesterday's closing price for the American-British exchange rate. At 11:00 a.m., it rose 0.0625 to $5.123125. It fluctuated slightly afterward. The price at 3:00 p.m. was $5.12125, which is lower than the opening price. Also, one US dollar equals 3 shillings and 10.864 pence.

British-French: Today (May 3rd), the opening price was 77.28 francs, the same as yesterday's price, and remained unchanged thereafter.

American-British: The New York-London exchange rate closed at 5.12625 yesterday, and opened at 5.12125 today. The first trade was 5.12125, the third trade was 5.1200, the fourth trade was 5.1200, the fifth trade was 5.1225, and the sixth trade was 5.12625. American-French was 6.6300.

Cotton and Wheat 94

American Cotton: Today (May 3rd), the cotton market opened relatively stable due to better telegraph from Liverpool. However, this bullish sentiment was offset by overnight sell orders. Later, the price rose slightly due to Liverpool buying and a strong silver market. Since then, sentiment has been mixed. Liverpool, Europe, the Far East, domestic, and manufacturers are all buying, while local New Orleans and the South are selling, offsetting each other.

Indian Cotton: Today (May 3rd), the Bombay cotton market remains bullish. Speculators are buying. The price of white cotton for July-August delivery is 193 rupees 25, up 5 pounds.

British Cotton: Today (May 3rd), the Liverpool cotton market. The price for July was 5.73 at 1:00 p.m., up 3 pounds from yesterday.

British Wheat: Today (May 3rd), the Liverpool wheat market. The price for July was 4 shillings and 4.125 pence at 1:00 p.m., the same as yesterday's closing price.

Rubber 95

London: Today (May 3rd), the rubber market situation is stable. At noon, the transaction price for July and September delivery was 7 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: Today (May 3rd), the rubber market situation is active and stable, due to the stable and higher prices in London. However, the opening surge was curbed by profit-taking. Sentiment is trending in multiple directions.

Securities 96

New York: Today (May 3rd), securities opened mixed. The volatility of some commodities, the uncertainty of future commercial trends, and the current developments in Washington are all unsettling forces. It is currently expected that there will not be a lasting rebound soon, but although the market situation was initially volatile, it then trended firm. Some stocks rose by one pound. Germany's Relief of Unemployment (Berlin Correspondence) Large-Scale Construction and Street Fundraising 118

The unemployment problem in Germany was a major issue during the Social Democratic Party's reign. Two years ago, there were signs of an economic alliance in the world, and the export of German goods showed a downward trend. At that time, the method of relieving unemployment was to rely on government spending for relief funds or unemployment insurance. However, the government did not have any alchemy itself, and its method of income was still to rely on public debt and taxes to pay for it. Once industry declined, finance stagnated, overseas exports decreased, and the pressure of debt increased, Germany had no choice but to let its unemployed increase day by day, and the economy was almost on the verge of collapse.

At the time when Hitler came to power (January of last year), the number of unemployed was about six million or more. As a result of the Hitler government's desperate efforts, by the autumn of last year, it had been reduced to 2.25 million people. However, this included seasonal factors, so from the winter of last year to the beginning of this year, the number of unemployed rose again to about 3.7 million people. Now the Hitler government is still taking this matter as its target. He wants to reduce the number of unemployed to less than two million people after the summer of this year.

The methods of reducing unemployment can be divided into two categories. One is a more serious attitude, and its business is also more

is of a permanent nature. The other one, although it is also concentrating spirit when working, always feels a bit comedic in nature, and the time limit is very short and it is not easy to continue.

The first type of method, first, is to build automobile roads. Germany is planning to become the first automobile country in Europe in the next two or three years. The government expects to build a six-thousand-kilometer automobile road network. These roads are all paved with asphalt and built quite carefully. In the past year, one thousand five hundred kilometers have been successfully built. However, how much effect these roads have on actual production, and how much effect they have in alleviating Germany's current economic panic, cannot but be questioned. The second is to open up wasteland, but this method of opening up wasteland is different from the masses. This is the coastal filling project and the irrigation project in the marshland. Build dikes far away on the seashore, expel the seawater within the scope of the dikes, and obtain land suitable for cultivation. This has already started on the North Sea coast, such as Frisia. Irrigating barren marshland properly will turn it into fertile land. It has already started near Hanover. Both of these projects are very large, requiring not only huge amounts of money, but also countless labor. Of course, these are not businesses that can be effective in the short term, and at the same time, Germany's unemployment problem cannot be completely resolved in the short term.

Secondly, it is temporary relief. The money raised by the first "Winter Relief Movement" that ended from last winter to March of this year totaled 320 million marks. From this, it can also be seen that the members of the National Socialist Party are too blatant. "Stormtroopers" are spread all over the streets and alleys to beg for donations. Even as soon as you go out, you will encounter donation team members. If you meet them and refuse to donate or escape home, you will be stigmatized as unpatriotic. Therefore, many people hide in their homes and dare not go out easily. There is also the so-called "One Dish Sunday," which means that on that Sunday's lunch, each person can only eat one dish. Afterwards, National Socialist Party members come out and collect fifty pfennigs from each household. In each restaurant, only one dish is allowed to be eaten, but it charges double the price. After gathering, the owner of the restaurant donates it. It is said that the total income of "One Dish Sunday" in Berlin is 400,000 marks. Another interesting thing is to restrict women's labor, and even prohibit both husband and wife from having a job together. The meaning of this is roughly based on ethical aspects, to return women to the path of being good wives and mothers as the main body, but the economic meaning of reducing unemployment is also there. And desperately encouraging marriage, all newly married people who form a family can get a long-term low-interest loan of one thousand marks from the government. This year, the Ministry of Finance budget has 250,000 marriage groups and is prepared with such a large marriage fund to lend to them. Also, those who have three children are exempted from repaying the loan. Furthermore, National Socialist Party members selling fabric flowers, linen badges, and glass badges pinned on their chests on the streets are also everywhere. This is also a means of relieving unemployment.

Draft Reform of Local Political System

Opinions from the Southwest, Believing that the Shortcomings of the Current System Cannot Be Reformed, Advocate Implementing the Provincial Governor System When Popularly Elected Provincial Governors are Elected 121

Guangzhou Correspondence, recently the Central Government proposed a draft to reform the local political system, changing the provincial committee system to the provincial governor system. The Southwest attached great importance to this and proposed research. After several discussions, it formulated opinions to review the draft, and on the 24th of this month, it was submitted to the 117th meeting of the Southwest Political Affairs Council. It was resolved to pass it and submit it to the Central Government for consideration and verification. The original text of the opinion on reviewing the draft reform of the local administrative system is recorded as follows: "It is verified that the provincial system should be formulated in accordance with the Prime Minister's system of balanced power. The meaning of this has been explained in detail in the preliminary review of the draft constitution, so it will not be discussed here. However, this draft is to reform the current provincial system, so the following opinions are based on the current actual situation. It is verified that the original intention of the original proposal is that the relationship between the current provincial and county system and the various competent ministries and commissions of the Central Government is unclear, the responsibility of the provincial committee system is not specific, the organization of the provincial government's various departments is huge, the political orders of the provincial government and the various competent departments are divergent, the organization of the provincial government itself is unreasonable, and the division of powers of the county government, the simplicity of the organization, and the inability to determine the county's finances, etc., are all sufficient to hinder the progress of administration, so a reform is proposed. It is judged whether this draft is appropriate, and it is still judged by whether it can improve the above-mentioned points. After carefully examining the first and second sections of Item A of the original draft, the original intention was to clearly define the relationship between the province and the various competent ministries and commissions of the Central Government, and the intention was indeed steady. However, this is only a legal issue and has nothing to do with the system. This regulation can be modified in the current provincial government organizational law, and there seems to be no need to involve the entire system. As for changing the provincial committee system to the provincial governor system, the intention of the original draft is to remedy the point of irresponsible management. However, this is only observed on the surface. If the drawbacks are exhausted, it not only goes against the purpose of pooling wisdom and benefiting from each other, but also once implemented, it is feared that the disadvantages will outweigh the advantages. The provincial government established three divisions: General Affairs, Civil Affairs, and Finance, and two departments: Education and Construction, as stipulated in Item 4. Except for the General Affairs Division, which is the renamed of the current provincial government secretariat, which is of no great importance and will not be discussed, it is verified that the two departments of Civil Affairs and Finance are relatively busy in most provinces. Therefore, when the provincial committee system was not implemented in the past, the Finance Department had been independently established. This is to adapt to the needs of the facts, which we cannot criticize. After examining the reform plan, the most important part was changed from a department to a division, while the two departments of Education and Construction, which have simpler affairs, still set up departments as usual, and clearly stipulate that they issue department orders. The current system is both messy and inconsistent, and it is even more untrue. It is also said in the original draft that the divergence of political orders between the current provincial government and the various competent departments is inherently incapable of being reformed, and it is even more feared that it may be intensified. The so-called reform is only sufficient to cause disturbances. The provincial government established a provincial assembly as stated in Item 8. Although the organization of the assembly was not mentioned, it is likely that it is a people's autonomous organization. If the provincial council is similar to the current provincial government committee meeting, it seems to have the nature of a provincial government administrative meeting. However, the original draft clearly stipulates that when the provincial assembly is adjourned, the provincial council will exercise its powers within a certain scope on its behalf, which is tantamount to the government exercising the powers of the people on its behalf. Although it is said that there are also members of the provincial assembly in the provincial council, the number of places is ultimately a minority. Is this method reasonable, it seems that there are still doubts. In summary, it is obvious that the various items listed in Item A of the original draft regarding the reform of the provincial system cannot reform the shortcomings of the current system as recognized in the original proposal. Even more telling, all provinces are now actively preparing for local autonomy, and recently there is a proposal to complete autonomy and end political tutelage within a limited time. As for the implementation of the provincial governor system, it is thought that it is better to wait until the local autonomy in each province is completed and implement it when the popularly elected provincial governors are elected than to rush to make meaningless reforms now. As for Item B, the reform of the county system, except for the fifth and sixth items, which relate to the county assembly and the county council, and the opinions on the eighth and ninth items of the reform of the provincial system are the same and have been detailed above, and will not be repeated. The remaining items are either not much different from the current system, or are merely changing the form without changing the substance, and are all of no great importance and will not be discussed." (April 24th)

Hubei Province Strictly Prohibits Opium, All Opium Dens in Wuhan Close Down in Compliance with Orders, Opium Poppy Seedlings in Northwestern Hubei are Uprooted by Armed Force 122

Hankou Correspondence, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek believes that the more opium prohibition is carried out over the years, the more rampant it becomes. Effective methods should be adopted and implemented on schedule. The former stationed in Hankou, the headquarters has promulgated various opium prohibition regulations, including (1) Prohibition of planting: Except for remote provinces such as Sichuan, Guizhou, and Yunnan, the inland provinces absolutely do not allow the planting of opium, and it is required to be uprooted within a limited time, so that no seedlings emerge from the soil. (2) Prohibition of smoking: Party, government, military service personnel, and students strictly undergo opium cessation and inspections. Young men and women are also not allowed to smoke freely. (3) Prohibition of transportation: Except for limited collection and transportation in remote provinces, no private individual or organization shall be allowed to transport it without authorization. (4) Prohibition of sale: Those who are granted licenses to operate soil paste shops must obtain licenses in accordance with the regulations, and must not set up branches or collude, especially prohibiting the lighting of lamps for people to smoke. The decree has been issued to all places long ago, but it has recently been found that opium dens are rampant in Hankou, and the number of opium addicts is increasing day by day. Young men and women are especially addicted to it. If the ban is not reiterated, there will never be a day to completely ban it. Therefore, on the 24th of last month, a telegram was sent to the chairman of the provincial government, Zhang Qun, and the director of the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office, Li Jihong, to close all opium dens in Wuhan by the end of last month. Even those who have already obtained licenses to operate soil paste shops are not allowed to light lamps for people to smoke. They are only allowed to sell soil paste in accordance with the regulations, and are not allowed to hang shop signs or post advertisements. Anyone under the age of forty is prohibited from smoking, and those who violate the rules will be punished. After receiving the order, Zhang and Li separately ordered their subordinates to comply. By the 30th, all opium dens in Wuhan had closed down in compliance with the order. The provincial government believes that the opium prohibition in various counties and cities should also adopt strict measures, and has ordered the Department of Civil Affairs to be responsible for handling it. In remote counties in western Hubei and northern Hubei, it has been found that many opium poppy seedlings are being planted privately. The Department of Civil Affairs will also preside over the armed uprooting, and those who violate the rules will be punished. (May 1st)

Northwest Inspection Notes - Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Geng Ya - The Garrison Cultivation in the Sui Area and the Baotou Industry 125

"The Yellow River has hundreds of harms, but the sole benefit is the Hetao." Everyone knows that the Hetao area has fertile soil and abundant water resources. However, the Sui District Garrison Cultivation Supervisory Office is the only organization that is actually engaged in planned and large-scale reclamation. Under the goal of "stationing troops for farming, developing the Northwest, and consolidating the border," the "soldier cultivation" that is actively being carried out has achieved commendable results and has the greatest hope. The Sui West Garrison Cultivation only began work in the last two or three years. Last year, a total of 1,300 hectares of land were reclaimed. This year, it is estimated that at least 1,700 hectares of land can be reclaimed. After three years of reclamation, there will definitely be huge harvests, and the results will be even more amazing. This can be known without divination. The Sui District Garrison Cultivation Committee is located in Taiyuan, and the Garrison Cultivation Supervisory Office is in Baotou. Yan Xishan, Director of the Jin-Sui Pacification, concurrently serves as the Supervisor. Zhang Yinwu, former Mayor of Beijing, Fu Zuoyi, Chairman of Suiyuan, and Wang Jingguo, Commander of the 70th Division, are the co-organizers, and Shi Huayan is the office manager. Yesterday, I visited the office and was received by Secretary Li Ganqing and Section Chief Liu Chao, who gave a detailed account of the general situation of land reclamation, as follows:

In the spring of the 20th year, Wang Jingguo, Commander of the 70th Division, led more than 80 demobilized officers and soldiers to form a reclamation team and purchased dozens of hectares of land in Wuyuan to cultivate. This was the initial step in the pilot soldier cultivation. The income from one year of cultivation was more than enough to maintain their lives. The officers and soldiers became more interested in their work. The following spring, they received the sympathy of Fu Zuoyi, Li Shumin, Shi Huayan, and others. Each division of the 70th, 72nd, and 73rd divisions allocated a company of soldiers, called the Pilot Soldier Cultivation Team, and established a Reclamation Joint Office, searching for more than 300 hectares of land in Linhe. In addition to cultivation, they also engaged in canal excavation, fortification construction, and new village construction. After the September 18th Incident, Director Yan made a comeback and was determined to "save the country through production," believing that only by devoting himself to productive enterprises could he save the country from peril. He then formed a Military Officer Garrison Cultivation Team with 500 demobilized military officers and established a Soldier Cultivation Pilot Office in Baotou, which carried out cultivation in Wuyuan. Later, the Sui District Reclamation Committee and the Supervisory Office were also established in Taiyuan and Baotou in the summer of the 21st year. The work implementation plan is divided into three phases. July to October of the same year is the investigation period. All land surveys, terrain measurements, and soil, product, and farming habit surveys have been implemented in groups. October to the following year (22nd year) February is the preparation period, that is, handling the dredging of river channels, purchasing agricultural tools, making cattle tools, seeds, and building materials. In the spring of the same year, three regiments of soldiers began cultivation. The autumn harvest was the pilot period, and at the same time, new villages were established, cooperation was promoted, and animal husbandry, afforestation, and road construction were carried out. A total of 1,300 hectares of land were reclaimed. Although it was the initial stage and there were natural disasters and wars, the harvest was not abundant, but it can be said that the pilot was successful. Therefore, this year, the scope was expanded and officially held, and entered the garrison cultivation implementation period. Everything is already on track, and progress is more convenient. It is planned to reclaim 1,700 hectares of land, which is not difficult to implement.

Mr. Sun Yat-sen keenly realized the danger that China had too many soldiers and no way to manage them, and advocated the soldier industry policy, advocating troop reductions. Now, Sui West is implementing garrison cultivation, turning soldiers into farmers. How will the future success be? Let's put it aside for now. However, at present, it can reduce the number of soldiers, make them manageable, transform unproductive people into productive people, "lay down the butcher knife and become a Buddha immediately." The success of the soldier cultivation policy is not only in its results.

Baotou's industry has never been developed. There are only two machine factories, both producing flour. One of them is the Electrical Appliance Flour Company, which also operates the city's electricity, and is relatively large in scale. I heard that Duan Shengwu, the responsible committee member of the company, is enthusiastic about Baotou's social welfare and the development of the Northwest. I made a special visit and received a warm reception. According to him, the company's capital is 300,000 yuan. It did not make a profit in the first three years, but now it is gradually showing good signs. There are a total of 100 employees. The highest wage for workers is 70 yuan, and the lowest is 20 yuan. Trainees receive 10 yuan. They can also study in their spare time. With such treatment, there have never been any labor disputes. The daily output of flour is 500 bags, each bag weighing 49 pounds. With the power of machines, 900 bags can be produced day and night, but there is no such consumption volume yet.

Duan was originally a division commander in Feng Yuxiang's army. Because he realized that "it is not a good way for Chinese soldiers not to be engaged in a profession," he resolutely broke away from military affairs and came here to devote himself to industry. In addition to operating the Electrical Appliance Flour Company, he also used his spare time to engage in three meaningful tasks: (1) Studying the Yellow River and piloting boat trips. The waterway between Baotou and Ningxia has been measured and a report has been written. It is believed that the Yellow River situation in Baoxi is comparable to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and can be used for boat trips. Preparations for boat trips are now being made. (2) Studying the agricultural situation in Hetao. Chinese people have failed in operating agriculture in Hetao one after another. There are more than 20 groups. The root cause is not the lack of land, labor, and capital conditions, but the responsible managers are selfish and harm things (examples are omitted due to space limitations). In order to understand the rural situation, he often goes to the countryside to conduct field investigations. (3) Organizing the Northwest Industry Mutual Aid Society. The purpose is to connect comrades who study practical problems in the Northwest, exchange knowledge, develop a spirit of mutual assistance, and jointly seek improvements in Northwest industry. Duan is amiable and simple. Few people who see him for the first time can recognize that he was once a soldier.

Zhu Jiqing, a member of the Central Committee, and An, a section chief of the Suiyuan Provincial Government, went to Wuyuan and Linhe to inspect the reclaimed land and returned to Baotou. They met with Mr. Duan Shengwu one after another. Several people who knew the situation in Hetao well were also present, and they talked freely about various situations as follows:

The soil in Hetao is as fine as flour. It is a pity that most of it has not been developed, and the land is abandoned. According to regulations, the purchase of Mongolian land should be handled by the Suiyuan Reclamation Bureau. However, ordinary land speculators take shortcuts, secretly give gifts and pay money to Mongolians, and arbitrarily purchase large areas, waiting for the price to sell, and still leave them barren. Last year's investigation showed that landlords owned large tracts of land, even up to 4,000 hectares. Some of the land is virgin land, and some is wasteland. When asked about the landlords, they are still far away in Tianjin and Peiping.

The land price is extremely low. Ordinary ocean coins can buy one hectare of land for 100 yuan. It may be difficult to get even one mu of land in other places. The highest price for each hectare in the area reclaimed by the Sui West Garrison Cultivation Supervisory Office is 120 yuan, the lowest is 60 yuan, and the average is 80 yuan. Once sold, the Reclamation Bureau and the Mongolian landlords each get 35%, and the remaining 30% is reserved for the Baotou office. Since the soil in Hetao is good and the land price is low, the number of barren land is increasing day by day. The reasons are very complicated. The main reason is the heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies. The tax collection here is unique. There is a so-called "measuring green to collect taxes," which means that taxes are collected if it is planted, otherwise it is not collected. The tax collection standards are difficult to determine clearly, and the collectors always manipulate it and exploit the people. In addition to paying the measuring green tax, farmers also have to pay various additional taxes that come with the occasion, such as the Qingmiao tax in Guyuan, which is as high as 70 yuan per hectare. Therefore, many farmers abandon their fields and disperse in all directions. (19th)

Anhui Province's New Budget Approved - Income and Expenditure Fall Short by 500,000 Yuan 127

Anqing Dispatch: Anhui Province's budget for the 23rd year was recently compiled by the Department of Finance, submitted to the Standing Committee of the Provincial Government for revision and approval, and reported to the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the Three Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui for review. It can be implemented once approved. The financial situation of Anhui Province has been in deficit for many years. The compilation of this new budget is not without hesitation. For example, it is difficult to abolish the organizations that existed last year. The only way is to set the standard that it does not exceed last year's budget. After repeated reductions by the competent authorities for the original plan, the total income and expenditure fall short by about 300,000 yuan. There are also debts due in the 22nd year, which should be repaid, about 200,000 yuan. The two together exceed 500,000 yuan. The income is a total of 1,040,000 yuan. The reliable funds are about 900,000 yuan in this province and 120,000 yuan in central coordination. Most of the rest is unreliable. Last year's expenditure was 1,080,000 yuan, and this year's expenditure is 1,130,000 yuan. In terms of the budget, there is a shortfall of 500,000 yuan, but in fact, there is a shortfall of more than 1,000,000 yuan. In addition, the expenses owed by various agencies recently have been about three months or more, and another 1,000,000 yuan is needed. If next year's budget is about 1,000,000 yuan longer, it can make up for last year's losses, and it can be said that income and expenditure are suitable. Otherwise, the new and old losses will be more than 2,000,000 yuan. It is difficult to rely on the central government to make up for this loss. The Department of Finance is now planning to deal with this difficult situation. In terms of expenditure, the new ones, non-essential uses, should be slowed down, and the old ones that can be reduced should be severely reduced, so that future income can make up for previous losses. (May 1st)

The Hengzhou Station of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Starts Construction 128

Hengyang News: The Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway project has been progressing rapidly recently. In addition to the extension of construction from both the north and south ends, the route has many large tunnels in the south and three major bridge projects, namely Yuan, Mi, and Lei Rivers in the north. The project is arduous. If we wait for the two ends to extend sequentially, it will delay the project. Therefore, the route south of Hengzhou was also approved by the Ministry of Railways and started construction ahead of schedule, forming a situation of three-sided simultaneous construction. A ceremony was held at the Caijiayuan station site on April 23 to commemorate the start of construction of the Hengzhou Station. People from all walks of life were invited to participate. On that day, there were dozens of representatives from Hengyang's military and political leaders, gentry, banks, and the press, as well as three to four thousand local people who participated freely, which was extremely grand. After playing music and setting off firecrackers, Director Ling presided over the meeting, performed the etiquette, and reported to the public on the construction of Hengzhou Station. Wen Bin, the magistrate of Hengyang County, and others gave speeches, giving deep support and encouragement. Then the groundbreaking ceremony was held, photos were taken and firecrackers were set off, and military music was melodious. That night, the bureau thanked the guests with a banquet and dispersed happily. The report of Director Zhou Ling of Zhuzhou-Shaoguan is recorded below: The Guangdong-Hankou Railway has been under discussion for nearly forty years since its initial proposal. It has gone through many twists and turns. The Guangzhou-Shaoguan section was completed in the fourth year of the Republic of China, and the Wuchang-Changsha section was completed in the seventh year of the Republic of China, and connected to the Zhuzhou section in the middle. The Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section, more than 450 kilometers in the middle, was suspended for more than ten years, and no one in our country did not look forward to the early completion of this road day and night. Among them, those who looked forward to it the most should be the people of Hunan and Guangdong provinces, and among the people of the two provinces, those who must be leading the way are our Heng people, which is beyond doubt. The reason why this road has been suspended for a long time is that the lack of an overall economic plan is the biggest reason. Fortunately, the central government has made the greatest determination to complete this road, and borrowed most of the British Gengkuan funds to complete it in four years. In order to speed up the construction, the bureau moved to Hengzhou from Guangzhou last autumn to coordinate the response. Now, in addition to the extension of construction from both ends, we are also simultaneously advancing southward from Hengzhou, with three sides starting at the same time, so as not to miss the government's deadline. The plan to start work in Heng has been realized today. Although the project held today is small, it is also a memorable event in the progress of the road construction of this road, and it is also a comfort to the desire of our Heng people. Hengzhou is located in the center of this road, about 542 kilometers south of Guangzhou and about 550 kilometers north of Wuchang. It is the hub of north-south transportation and an important commercial port in central Hunan. In the future, it will be celebrated that the branch line will be completed and the Hong-Gui Highway will be extended, then the traffic between Guizhou and Guangxi provinces and the mainland of the Yangtze River, and the exchange of special products from various provinces, will all gather here. Therefore, Hengzhou Station occupies the most important position in the entire line. Although it is temporarily listed as a second-class station, it may develop into a first-class station in the future. In the early stage of the creation, we can't help but look a little further ahead to avoid difficulties in the future. Therefore, the selection of the location, the layout of the station and all equipment, are all aimed at developing commerce and facilitating travel, and are carefully studied before being submitted to the Ministry for approval. As for the detailed situation in the station, a booklet has been compiled separately, describing the station planning, site selection equipment and the use of land and other items, and distributed to all walks of life for reference, which will not be repeated here. The Ministry of Railways recently believes that the relationship of this road is extremely important and is making every effort to allocate funds to allow the road to be completed slightly ahead of schedule. Also, because the pound price has fallen, the current fund portion of Gengkuan has been greatly affected. The Bureau was ordered to make the most stringent plan, with the principle of first connecting the rails and then supplementing the equipment. Our bureau is now implementing all construction projects in accordance with this principle, with the goal of connecting the rails by the end of the 25th year of the Republic of China, and the construction aspects are seeking to have a solid and permanent road. As for the completeness of the equipment, it still needs to wait until after the opening of the road, so that the road can be connected as soon as possible with the limited funds. The colleagues of the Bureau feel that they bear a heavy responsibility and are deeply afraid of overstepping. Mutual assistance and support are waiting to be clarified. Today, in the opening ceremony, what makes us deeply uneasy is the matter of using civilian land and moving graves and demolishing houses. This matter was deeply concerned at the beginning of the Bureau's design, and efforts were made to minimize the impact on the people and minimize the relocation of graves and the demolition of houses. However, because Jiangdong Town is close to Heng City, the loss is inevitable. Judging from our country's old ideas, the colleagues of the Bureau are extremely sorry, but the railway is ultimately a major national transportation plan, and it is inevitable to achieve public needs with a small number of inconveniences. The Bureau is now repeatedly urging the prudent handling of all the land and mu collected this time for public affairs, and giving preferential land prices, and issuing cash immediately. For those who are requisitioned land, before the actual requisition, the landowners without contracts will be notified in advance to pay the price, and the local government will be proved to be exempt from tax to alleviate the people's difficulties, in order to reduce the pain to the least possible in the inevitable sacrifice. The Bureau has never been deeply sympathetic to those who are requisitioned for fields and houses due to road construction. Today's ceremony is over, and we will invite all the guests to hold the groundbreaking ceremony, and then the construction will officially start. I deeply hope that the road construction of this road can proceed smoothly with the blessing of all of you, and especially hope that you will not hesitate to teach us in the future and use it to correct our mistakes. Please forgive me for the inadequate reception today.

Songjiang - The Songsi Ferry Was Searched Midway 129

The Songsi Xin Da Ferry, operated by Ma Abba, arrived in Songjiang from Si on the afternoon of April 25. On the way, near Jiuliting, a member of the Second Squadron of the Water Police Department boarded the ship in plain clothes. When the ship arrived at Wulitang, the plainclothes water police suddenly blew a whistle and forced the captain to stop. At the same time, many water police officers from the department, who had been prepared on the shore, each took out a box gun and forced the ship to shore. The passengers dispersed in shock. After a while, a small package of so-called red pills was found in the passenger cabin. Without asking the reason, the captain Dong Changming and the tugboat operator Jin Ayou were immediately detained and escorted to the Songjiang team headquarters for torture. Dong Changming and others were injured and have filed a complaint with the Songjiang County Court Prosecutor's Office for questioning. Unexpectedly, in the early morning of the 30th, the department sent its armed personnel to Si again, robbed the Xin Da Ferry, and arrested three crew members. That afternoon, the department sent its personnel to Si again, intending to rob and detain the Xu Si Ban De Ferry, because the ship was also operated by Ma Abba. People in Si were very unhappy. Later, various local agencies came forward to intervene and stop it, which avoided a city-wide strike.

County Government Strictly Investigates Bribery in the Red Pill Case 136

Lu Chongpeng, the "Red Pill King" of this county, on January 31st of last year, transported a large quantity of red pills from Fuan Town in the 9th District to the county. While passing in front of the Farmers' Education Center in Sanyang Town, 6th District, he was discovered by members of the 6th District Corps and sent to the district headquarters for investigation. However, Gu Tianming, the leader of the district corps, colluded with Yang Zuoyuan, the director of corps affairs, and released both the person and the goods after receiving a bribe. The incident was uncovered by the Jianghai Daily, which first reported it, attracting the attention of people throughout the county. After the county party headquarters sent personnel to investigate and confirm the facts, and after representatives of the people of the 6th District, such as Shi Zhili, filed a complaint with the county government, Lu Chongpeng, Gu Tianming, and Yang Zuoyuan were repeatedly summoned by the county, but they refused to appear in court. Subsequently, Gu and Yang were dismissed from their positions by the Provincial Security Committee for failing to properly handle security (Yang is now working for the tax police in Chongming, and Gu is working as a section member in the Liyang County government), resulting in the case remaining unresolved. The county government has now scheduled a continuation of the trial on May 12th and has already signed warrants ordering the police to strictly arrest Lu, Gu, and Yang and bring them to justice for interrogation. The situation is quite serious.

Wuxi: Extortion Attempt Foiled, Arrest Made on the Spot 139

Gui Xiangcun Teashop, located at No. 1 East Street, Dashiqiao Tuen, in the city, has been open for more than ten years. The owner, Li Pan'gen, has quite a bit of savings. He has a son named Shengshi, who is thirteen years old and attends Peixin Elementary School. Unexpectedly, on March 11th, 14th, and April 21st (Gregorian calendar), Pan'gen suddenly received three threatening letters signed by Zhang Jingqiao, a Communist Wu Xuexia, demanding 100 silver dollars and instructing him to wrap the money in black paper and place it in the broken wall hole of the Lingguan Temple on April 30th; otherwise, Shengshi would be killed. Li was shocked upon receiving the letter and immediately discussed it with Gu Renquan, who lived to the west of his house. On that day, they purchased 150 yuan of counterfeit banknotes from Yantong Bank and attached a letter, advising him to repent. They placed them together in the broken wall hole of the Lingguan Temple. At the same time, they agreed with Gu Renquan and others to wait nearby. At around 2:00 AM, someone went to retrieve the money and was immediately captured. Upon inspection, it was found to be Pan Da, the son of Yang Shunshi, the owner of Yang Yuqi Paint Shop at No. 54 nearby. Subsequently, one person who was keeping watch nearby was also arrested, who turned out to be Han Chang (also known as A'er), the son of Yang Zibin, the owner of Yang Yuanxing Paint Shop at No. 55, and Pan Da's cousin. Li Pan'gen was extremely surprised to see this, as they were all long-time neighbors. He wondered why they had done this. Considering that they were ignorant and had accidentally gone astray, he felt that there were extenuating circumstances, so he did not intend to investigate further. However, the matter had already been learned by the detectives Wang Shuanglin, Xu Kunsheng, and Zhang Biao of the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, who took Yang Pan Da and Yang Han Chang brothers to the bureau for questioning. After being interrogated by Wu, a section member, they were transferred to the local court's prosecutor's office yesterday. After the prosecutor, Ren, opened a court for interrogation, he ordered Yang Pan Da and Yang Han Chang to be detained. The plaintiff, Li Pan'gen, and others were ordered to return home and await further action.

Director Zhou Inspects Education 140

Director Zhou Fohai of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, accompanied by Section Chiefs Xiang Jutan, Chen Xifang, Editing Director Yi Junzuo, and General Affairs Director Tian Yuelong, came to Wuxi on the 30th of last month to inspect the educational situation. On the 1st of this month, Mr. Zhou diligently traveled to the city and countryside to inspect the Educational Institute and the Huibei Experimental District, the Beixia Experimental District's first branch, and then went to inspect Dongting Elementary School, the Beixia District Headquarters, and Nanqian Elementary School. On the morning of the 2nd, Mr. Zhou departed from the Educational Institute and rushed to inspect the Provincial Wuxi Normal School, the National Studies Training Institute, and the County Junior High School. Finally, guided by Director Zang of the Education Bureau and others, he went to inspect the Jingzhi Girls' School in Beichan Temple Alley, the Ximen Public Sports Field, Mianhua Lane Elementary School, and Huishan Elementary School, and gave instructions to each school. That evening, he convened a meeting of all faculty and staff at the Provincial Normal School auditorium, stating briefly that in terms of moral education, a person's knowledge and character are equally important. Many people have high intelligence, but their character has many flaws, which is the main reason for the failure of Chinese education. In the future, special attention should be paid to moral education. Teachers should treat students like their own children, with the heart of a loving mother and the methods of a strict father. This is the best model for moral education. In terms of educational affairs, junior high schools should follow the rules and progress step by step, and senior high schools should pay attention to practical work, etc. Yesterday (the 3rd), Mr. Zhou inspected the County Library, the Mass Education Center, the Central Elementary School, the County Girls' Junior High School, and the County First and Second schools, etc., and is scheduled to go to Luoshe today to inspect the Rural Teachers' School.

Zhenjiang: Jiangsu Construction Department Sends Personnel to Inspect the Liutang River Project 141

The Jiangsu Construction Department believes that the completion of the Liutang River is of great importance to the farmland in northern Jiangsu. Since the start of construction in January of this year, they have been actively proceeding and sparing no effort. Sections of the project have either been fully completed or are 80-90% completed. However, the Donghai and Guanyun sections were initially delayed due to the county magistrate's lack of effort in conscripting labor, and the provincial government has already dismissed him and ordered the newly appointed county magistrate to oversee and urge the work to facilitate progress. Furthermore, because the Liu Guitang bandit gang harassed Ganyu, the defenses north of Dongguan were strained, and the project was again delayed. Recently, in the Donghai area, the construction of the embankment has been largely completed, and the excavation work is also progressing rapidly and will likely be completed on schedule. However, the Guanyun section is located downstream of the entire project. If it cannot be completed at the same time, the middle reaches will be affected, which is of great importance to the entire project. In order to take the entire project into account, the Liutang River Project Office has transferred the Lianshui labor force to help Guanyun first excavate the downstream area. After the downstream excavation is completed, they will jointly excavate the riverbed in the Lianshui section. At this critical juncture, in order to ensure the project's success, the Construction Department has dispatched Xiao Kaiying, the section chief of the First Section in charge of water conservancy, to conduct an inspection and provide guidance on everything, in order to ensure smooth completion.

Yangzhou: Salt Workers in Twelve Forts Petition 142

Through the suggestions and arrangements of Salt Commissioner Miao, the salt transport of Lianghuai, regarding the salt transport to Hunan, Hubei, Western Anhui and other coasts, will gradually be changed from sailing transport to steamship transport, so that the salt of all provinces can reduce freight costs and reach the coast quickly. Therefore, the lives of more than 100,000 sailing transport workers and sailors in the Twelve Forts of Yizheng have become insecure, and they are extremely panicked. Representatives were previously elected and repeatedly appealed to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Salt Affairs Administration, and the Nanchang Chiang Kai-shek's Headquarters, but no satisfactory results were obtained. As a result, 600-700 sailships that could be transported were accumulated in the Twelve Forts, which also had a great impact on the market in the fort. The provincial government also believes that the salt transport favors steamship transport, and the loss of employment for sailing transport workers and the lack of food is having a great impact on local security and social economy. It should maintain the proportion of 5 steamships and 8 sailships, and at the 653rd provincial government meeting, Commissioner Wang Bailing was sent to Beijing to contact the Ministry of Finance. After hearing the news, the fort residents specially sent representatives from the 18 gangs of workers and sailors to Yangzhou to visit Commissioner Wang through the introduction of Bao Xiangzhong, a fellow villager in Yangzhou, to state the situation of unemployment of sailships, and that sail transport does not hinder public tax revenue, merchants' capital, etc., and asked them to convey the suffering and argue on the basis of reason. Commissioner Wang has agreed to forward the matter to the capital.

Southwest Route Trial Flight Successful 150

Reportedly, in November of last year, the company sent Nie Kaiyi, the director of the aviation group, along with pilot An Lisheng, to depart from Hankou, pass through Changsha, Guangzhou, Longzhou, and Kunming, and return to Chongqing, in order to open up air transport between Hunan, Hubei, Yunnan, and the two Guangdongs. After Longzhou, due to accidentally landing in Annam, they were once detained by the French authorities. After requesting release by telegram, they were able to fly safely to Yunnan. It was supposed to be officially opened to navigation on a specific date, but due to funding issues, it has been delayed until now, and there is still no concrete plan. The exact date of the opening is currently uncertain.

Sichuan-Tibet Route Actively Being Prepared 151

The Sichuan-Tibet route is being planned by the company upon the order of the Ministry of Communications. It involves aviation from Sichuan to Lhasa, Tibet. It is believed that there are many mountains and ridges in these two places, making flying quite difficult. Therefore, the section from Sichuan via Badong to Kangding is being opened first. The airports in both places have been telegraphed by the Ministry of Communications to Liu Xiang and Liu Wenhui to be built on their behalf. A reply has been received agreeing to do so. As soon as funding is available, trial flights can begin.

Search for Missing Aircraft Abandoned 153

As for the missing No. 17 aircraft, although remains of the aircraft have been discovered successively last month, the bodies have not been recovered to date. It is unknown whether they have any effect. The families of the passengers and pilots have also not made any representations to the company. In recent days, due to the search for the aircraft, the company has suffered considerable losses. It has now decided to abandon the search and wait for the truth to come out.

Both Routes Still Flying Yesterday 154

According to the Min Yan News Agency, the China National Aviation Corporation reported yesterday that although the weather was bad yesterday, with wind and rain all day long, there was no heavy fog. The company's Shanghai-Ping and Shanghai-Hankou routes were still operating as usual. The planes flying north from Shanghai to Ping and west to Hankou have all arrived safely. As for the plane that flew south from Ping the day before yesterday, a fire broke out midway through Tianjin. After being extinguished, the damage was minor and it has been repaired. It flew directly to its destination and arrived here at 6:00 PM that evening.

Huang Jintao to Sail to Europe on the 6th: Discussing the Mission and Purpose of the Inspection (Four Items) 155

According to the Central News Agency, Huang Jintao, the Director of the Mining Department of the Ministry of Industry, who has been appointed to go to Europe and the United States to inspect mining and steel matters, is scheduled to depart on the Empress of Canada on the 6th. According to him, the mission and purpose of his trip to Europe and the United States can be divided into four items: 1. To investigate the plant price of the proposed state-owned central steel plant; 2. To investigate the aluminum manufacturing industry. To investigate the evolution of the human race, which has evolved from the Stone Age to the Bronze Age to the Steel Age. But now the Steel Age is about to shift to the Aluminum Age. The Altmiune aluminum manufacturing industry is a new industry. Aluminum has many uses and has now partially replaced the position of steel. For example, most household appliances are made of pure aluminum because they are light and do not rust. As for freight cars, some are now made of aluminum alloys, whose strength is equal to that of steel, but they are two-thirds lighter than steel. Also, for building houses, manufacturing automobiles, and airplane wings, as well as daily furniture and utensils, Duralumin, an aluminum alloy, is used because it is light and has the same strength as steel. The world's major iron ore mines have been developed, and they are being used very quickly. China's iron ore is especially not abundant. Therefore, it is currently urgent for our country to revitalize the aluminum manufacturing industry. The Ministry of Industry has designated Shandong's abundant aluminum mines as a reserve area. Therefore, he is specifically investigating the aluminum manufacturing industries of various countries in order to formulate our country's aluminum manufacturing plan. 3. To investigate the industry of extracting gasoline from brown ash. China's oil reserves are limited, and the expansion of highways in recent years has made it necessary to strive for self-sufficiency in gasoline, otherwise the leakage will be very large. Currently, most countries extract gasoline from brown ash by low-temperature distillation. It is urgently necessary for our country to follow suit. Therefore, an investigation must be conducted and a plan for implementation must be formulated. 4. To investigate the industry of extracting gasoline from coal using light chemical hydrogenation. Our country's oil fields are not abundant. Unless various methods are used to extract gasoline or other oil materials, we cannot be self-sufficient. Germany currently has new factories using light chemical hydrogenation to extract gasoline from coal. This must also be investigated incidentally in order to implement it in our country. It is said that Mr. Huang's inspection will take about four months, and he will return to the country immediately.

Ministry of Industry Subsidizes Domestic Coal: Will Reduce Costs and Freight for Mine Owners 156

According to the Central News Agency, in response to the decline of the domestic coal market, a relief measure was implemented in October of last year to increase the import tax on foreign coal. The impact of the tax increase is enough to prevent Japanese coal from being dumped again. According to those familiar with the coal market, Japanese coal sales this year have decreased by one-tenth compared to before October of last year. Kailuan coal took the opportunity to develop. Because its sales in the Northeast are very small, it is urgently promoting sales in Guannei. Kailuan coal has lower costs and freight than domestic coal, so it is easy to occupy the market. As a result, domestic coal has lower production and higher costs, making it unable to compete, and its future is becoming increasingly precarious. In view of this, the Ministry of Industry held a meeting to discuss relief measures, and has sent personnel to Henan Province to investigate coal production conditions, try to reduce costs for mine owners, and will negotiate with the Ministry of Railways to reduce freight in order to provide relief.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Assigns Engineer Trainees

Scheduled to Sail to England: Six to Depart on the 20th of This Month 157

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is using Sino-British Boxer Indemnity funds to build four ocean-going vessels, which have been named Haiyuan, Haiting, Haili, and Haizhen, etc. As the first vessel is scheduled to be completed in September and come to Shanghai to operate on the South China route, the company has specifically sent Captain Ma Jiajun, Teng Shibiao, Technician Huang Zonglun, Chief Engineer Zhang Guoquan, and two junior third engineers, and two students from the Wusong Merchant Marine School to England to practice driving and engine management, etc. The company had submitted a report to the Ministry of Communications for instructions. It was originally planned to sail to Europe in early April, but because the Ministry's order had not been issued for a long time, the members were unable to depart. The Ministry's approval was only received the day before yesterday.

Six members will depart first. The six members of the company's delegation to England include naval technologist Huang Zonglun, chief engineer Zhang Guoquan from Jiahe ship, and two second-class apprentice engineers Li Changwen and Shi Ruichang, as well as two students from the Marine Engineering Department of Wusong College. The captains Ma and Teng will go to England in July to take over the ships. The Ministry has approved the company's overseas procedures, and the necessary travel expenses have been readied for those six members, totaling 30,000+ yuan. All six members were notified the day before yesterday from the marine department to prepare everything before their sailing overseas. The company marine department and the crew leaving for England for practical training are scheduled to leave this month, because each of the crew has duties to be done, and it has been ordered that they quickly tie up all loose ends and come to an end. At the same time, a letter has been sent to Wusong Commercial Vessel School, asking that they present the list of two selected trainees to the company, so that tickets and the like can be processed. After consultation, it was decided that they would depart from Shanghai on the twentieth of this month, and a telegram has been sent to England to notify Wu Daming and Shi Gan to notify the shipyard, so that they can contact them in advance.

Restrictions on Filipinos Visiting the United States 159

The bill stipulates that Filipinos entering the United States must be subject to the same restrictions as other foreigners, with an annual quota of only fifty people. Once the bill is passed in Manila, it must be implemented immediately. When the President Hoover sailed to the United States, there were 160 Filipino passengers on board. Whether U.S. immigration officials can allow them to land in San Francisco is a serious issue. Public opinion may not be lenient enough to let them go.

Indian Anti-British Protester Sentenced: Gam Xin Sentenced to Imprisonment; Shouted Slogans When Hearing the Verdict 160

According to the Zi Lin Daily, Gam Xin, 32, committed sedition in Shanghai in August 1929 and was deported back to India by the British authorities. He returned to China in September 1932 and was wanted by the British authorities until he was arrested in Hankou on April 18 of this year and sent to Shanghai for trial. Yesterday morning, the British Consular Court sentenced him to two months' imprisonment, after which he would still be deported back to India. At the time of the verdict, the prisoner shouted, "Down with the British!", "Long live Hindustan!", and "Long live the revolution!" without end.

Establishment of Branch Customs Posts for Civilian Vessels in Various Locations: Jianghai Customs Notice 163

Jianghai Customs issued a notice yesterday stating: "Regarding the establishment of branch customs posts for the management of civilian vessels in Qinhuangdao, Miaodao, Weihaiwei, and Shidao, it is now in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance to establish them starting June 16th of this year. From this date forward, all civilian vessels engaged in foreign trade (including domestic trade vessels carrying goods subject to import duties) must comply with the following measures for managing civilian vessels and must not violate them: (A) 1. Civilian vessels sailing from Dalian (Kwantung Leased Territory), the puppet state of Manchukuo, and foreign locations to any coastal area between Qinhuangdao and Longkou must report and be inspected at either the Qinhuangdao or Miaodao customs post. Before reporting and being inspected at either of these posts, they must not sail past the line running from Qinhuangdao through the Miaodao branch customs post to the Shandong coast in the west. 2. Civilian vessels sailing from within the Bohai Bay, the puppet state of Manchukuo, or the western coast of the Kwantung Leased Territory (north of Laotieshantou) to coastal areas outside the area between Qinhuangdao and Longkou must report and be inspected at the Miaodao branch customs post. Those sailing to areas south of the southeastern corner of Shandong Cape must report and be inspected at both the Miaodao and Shidao branch customs posts. 3. Civilian vessels sailing from any location on the southeastern coast of Dalian, between Laotieshantou and Dalian: (甲) Those sailing to any location on the northeastern coast of Shandong, east of Longkou and west of Weihaiwei, must report and be inspected at the Miaodao branch customs post. (乙) Those sailing to Weihaiwei or any coastal area between Weihaiwei and Shidao must report and be inspected at the Weihaiwei branch customs post. (丙) Those sailing to Shidao or any location south of Shidao must report and be inspected at the Shidao branch customs post. 4. Civilian vessels sailing from the eastern coast of the Kwantung Leased Territory (east of Dalian) and the coastal area of the puppet state of Manchukuo along the Yalu River Bay: (甲) Those sailing to any coastal area between Longkou and Shidao may report and be inspected at either the Miaodao or Weihaiwei branch customs posts at their convenience. (乙) Those sailing to Shidao or any location south of Shidao must report and be inspected at the Shidao branch customs post. 5. Civilian vessels sailing from the Korean coastal area north of an imaginary line extending eastward from Shidao to the full extent of the line to any coastal area between Longkou and Shidao may report and be inspected at either the Weihaiwei or Shidao branch customs posts at their convenience. 6. Civilian vessels sailing from Korea or other foreign locations to areas north of Shidao, whose routes pass through the imaginary line extending eastward from Shidao, must report and be inspected at the Shidao branch customs post. If sailing to any coastal area between Longkou and Qinhuangdao, they must report and be inspected at both the Shidao and Miaodao branch customs posts. All civilian vessels traveling on the above routes, regardless of whether they have sailed to other locations in China or have reported and been inspected at other coastal customs posts in China, must report and be inspected at the designated management branch customs posts mentioned above. (B) All civilian vessels going to any of the above management branch customs posts to report and be inspected must follow the following procedures: 1. They must present their civilian vessel registration certificate and shipping permit, as well as various documents issued by the Maritime Administration Bureau, for inspection. 2. They must submit two copies of the cargo manifest, filling in the following items in detail: (1) Name of the agent store, (2) Brand or identification number, (3) Registration number, (4) Name and type of the vessel, (5) Name of the shipowner, (6) Name of the owner, (7) Tonnage, (8) Place of origin, (9) Date of departure, (10) Date of entry, (11) Destination, (12) Cargo mark or brand, (13) Number of items, (14) Packaging style, (15) Type of goods, (16) Weight, (17) Value, (18) Consignee, (19) Remarks. 3. If the head of the management branch customs post deems it necessary to conduct a detailed inspection of the cargo carried by the civilian vessel, the civilian vessel must immediately comply with the order to be inspected. (4) After the management branch customs post inspects all the documents of the civilian vessel, except for the registration certificate, which will be stamped and returned to the shipowner for safekeeping for customs patrol vessels to inspect at any time, all other documents will be placed in a sealed envelope, sealed, and stamped, and also given to the civilian vessel to carry. They must be presented in their original sealed state to the customs branch post at the designated unloading and tax payment location. (C) If a customs branch post or customs patrol vessel finds that a vessel traveling on the routes listed in item A has passed through a management branch customs post without reporting and being inspected, it shall be immediately treated as smuggling and punished according to regulations. (D) If a civilian vessel reports to a customs branch post a designated destination, and it is later discovered that the vessel has secretly unloaded goods at a location other than the reported destination, or violates the regulations governing navigation of civilian vessels as recorded in the registration certificate, it shall be punished according to the severity of the offense, as stipulated in those regulations. (E) These measures are provisional and may be revised at any time if there are any omissions. All civilian vessel personnel must be informed. This notice is hereby issued." May 2, 1934. Supervisor Tang Haian, Tax Commissioner Bode.

The United States Regularly Holds

International Petroleum Exposition 164

According to news from the U.S. Commercial Counselor's Office in this city, the eighth International Petroleum Exposition will be held in Tulsa, Oklahoma, USA, from May 12th to 19th of this year. The first session was held in 1923. Its scale is unparalleled among industrial exhibitions in the United States, and perhaps not many can match it in the world. The U.S. government has already issued formal invitations from the State Department to foreign governments to participate as scheduled. The International Petroleum Exposition is not for profit. Its mission is entirely to promote the interests of the industry. When the meeting was held in 1930, 1,500 petroleum companies from various places participated, and 150,000 people visited during the eight days of public exhibition. The U.S. Congress has passed resolutions four times, authorizing the Secretary of State to invite the 48 states of the United States and friendly nations to participate. This year, it will be held as usual. At the 1930 exhibition, 73 representatives from 21 countries traveled from afar to attend. The exhibition items of this conference will cover all aspects related to the production, transportation, refining, and sales of petroleum. The "Science and Technology Committee" of the conference will also publicly display various scientific instruments and specimens to arouse the interest of petroleum merchants and the public. The content of the petroleum industry is vast, with countless branches and ramifications. Anyone who wants to get a glimpse of the entire industry in a short time should not miss this excellent opportunity.

A total of 42,700 bags of flour were involved. Due to the military transportation disruptions in northern and western Fujian and the difficulty of mailing, the documents could not be submitted to the department within the stipulated tax refund period. It should have been handled according to the original case to maintain uniformity. However, considering the Fujian Incident, which was a special circumstance, the stated reasons for the delay were not without merit. In view of the consideration for merchants, this department will make an exception this time. Starting from the date of receipt of the documents by this department, the 24,700 bags of flour that were overdue for less than one month will be approved for delivery to the Fuzhou Consolidated Tax Administration for verification and refund. The remaining 18,000 bags of flour, which were overdue for more than one month, should be excluded and will not be refunded. The previous request is approved. In addition to instructing the Fuzhou Administration to verify and reply, the remaining documents are returned with this letter for your reference and notification."

The Jiangsu Construction Department Revises the Regulations on Silk Cocoon Guilds

Wuxi and Other Counties Must Switch to Using Cocoon Drying Machines: Shanghai Silk Merchants Schedule a Meeting to Discuss Cocoon Purchases 167

With the cocoon season approaching, silk merchants everywhere are actively preparing to purchase cocoons. Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are the main cocoon-producing areas in China. The Sericulture Management Improvement Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Department of Construction has specially formulated thirteen articles of regulations on silk cocoon guilds and ordered them to be implemented in various counties. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency has learned the gist of the regulations from silk organizations as follows: The Jiangsu Sericulture Management Improvement Committee believes that merchants' applications for cocoon licenses are not accurate. Therefore, those with licenses but without stoves (for drying cocoons) will have their licenses revoked, and those with stoves but without licenses will be ordered to close. Those who report less than they have or more than they have will be investigated. It is also stipulated that Wuxi and other counties will be designated as model areas, and all cocoon guilds must switch to using cocoon drying machines, which must be implemented by May 1935. A registration fee of three yuan will be collected for each dan (unit of weight) of dried cocoons, and twelve yuan will be charged for silkworm eggs and for improving the sericulture industry. As for the silk merchants in this city, they will schedule a meeting to discuss cocoon purchases.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Responds to the Pilot Association

Explanation of the Recovery of Pilotage Rights: Misunderstandings in the Pilot Association's Statements 168

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Shanghai Pilot Association, stating that the recent establishment of a pilotage management committee by the Chinese government conflicted with the association's vested rights. To protect its own interests, the association requested three matters from the government and asked the chamber of commerce to forward them to the government for assistance. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that there are some misunderstandings in the association's statements and has responded with a letter explaining the significance of recovering pilotage rights. The following is an excerpt of the original text: "The use of native pilots is a common practice in all countries of the world. Although the nationalities of your association's members are not uniform, if you carefully examine the methods practiced in your respective countries, you will know that this move is not an innovation of the Chinese government. Moreover, Article 8 of the recently promulgated regulations of the pilotage management committee stipulates that 'If there are not enough qualified pilots in a port to meet the pilotage quota, the pilotage management committee shall select experienced Chinese pilots and grant them practice certificates to serve on a trial basis.' Furthermore, the change to using Chinese pilots is limited to future vacancies and does not affect the business of your association's members. Therefore, while the Chinese government's legislation strives to conform to international practice, it also makes every effort to take care of the current situation and the interests of your association's members. If we criticize it from a third-party perspective, we would also say that this measure is extremely fair. As for your association's claim that there are no people familiar with port affairs on the Chinese side, and therefore we have to rely on foreigners, this is based on a document submitted by Robert Hart, the former Inspector General of Customs, to the Yamen (Foreign Affairs Office). This association believes that your association's judgment does not fully accord with the facts. Let's set that aside for now, but it must be known that the Chinese government is adopting a gradual approach in using native pilots, so qualified personnel can be gradually cultivated and be fully sufficient. Although the ships sailing in the ports now are not just from China, the goods they carry and the passengers they transport are mostly Chinese, and the interests of China are most affected. The Chinese government will not disregard the selection of pilots. However, these arguments do not seem to be the main points of your letter. Your association's main requests are three: (1) The pilotage management committee must be well-organized and highly disciplined, just like the former Marine Department. (2) The committee must truly understand the hardships and dangers of sailors. Although there is no responsibility on the part of the government or the committee to respond to these two points, we would like to tell your association from the perspective of this association that the committee is composed of one Customs Tax Commissioner, one Harbour Master, and one representative from the Harmony Chamber of Commerce, originally to make it easier to get things done, and it is easier for your association to contact them for requests. In addition, the Ministry of General Staff, the Ministry of the Navy, the Ministry of Communications, and this association each send a representative. These four representatives are all navigation experts. This association does not see anything unhealthy in its organization, nor does it see anything unclear about the hardships of sailors. The current isolation is due to your association's adherence to decades of established ideas and the failure of the Harmony Chamber of Commerce to send a representative. If Chinese and foreign personnel can gather together to discuss matters regularly, these doubts will naturally be dispelled. (3) The pilotage property rights should be protected. This association believes that although the Chinese government has always recovered its rightful sovereignty based on international conventions, it has never confiscated the property rights of foreigners or failed to protect them. Your association need not worry too much about this. Furthermore, in our opinion, your association can submit its requests to the management committee. If the committee does not respond to anything within its power, we can forward it to the government on your behalf. If you deny the existence of the committee and expect this association to help, then this association is not willing to comply. Addressed to the Shanghai Pilot Association."
