The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests an Explanation

Method of Re-Electing Alternate Committee Members of the Chamber of Commerce: Is a Re-Election Required Every Term? 170

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday, requesting an explanation of the method of re-electing alternate committee members of the Chamber of Commerce. The original text reads: "Article 15 of the Implementing Rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law states that 'The Chamber of Commerce may, in accordance with its articles of association, elect alternate committee members when electing the Executive Committee or Supervisory Committee. When there is a vacancy, they shall be elected to fill the position in order of succession, and their term of office shall be limited to completing the term of the former member.' According to this provision, the alternate committee members should be re-elected at the same time each time the Chamber of Commerce holds an election, that is, when the law stipulates that half of the members should be re-elected every two years. Also, the term of office of alternate committee members is to complete the term of the former member. Therefore, alternate committee members themselves do not have a term of office until they are elected to fill a vacancy. The intention of the four-year term for the executive and supervisory committee members, with half of the members being re-elected every two years, is to mix new and old members so that they can handle matters smoothly. It does not seem applicable to alternate committee members, because alternate committee members do not hold a position until they are elected to fill a vacancy. Furthermore, the letter from the Judicial Yuan No. 913 to the Central People's Movement Committee in 1933 also states that 'According to the current law, there is no provision for re-electing half of the alternate executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce. Therefore, there is no need to re-elect them when the executive and supervisory committee members are re-elected by lottery for the first time.' According to this interpretation, it can also be considered that, except for the first lottery, the alternate committee members do not need to be re-elected along with the re-elected members. However, each time an election is held thereafter, the alternate committee members should be entirely re-elected, because the provisions of Article 15 of the Implementing Rules only state that alternate committee members should be re-elected, and do not mention the re-election of half of them. In fact, there are as many as seven alternate executive committee members and as many as three alternate supervisory committee members. If all of them are elected to fill vacancies within two years, then there is no reason to elect only half of them in the next election. Therefore, the legal text does not say 're-elect half of them,' but 're-elect,' precisely to avoid any obstruction. If the above statement is correct, then the half of the alternate executive and supervisory committee members who were re-elected in June 1932 due to the first lottery and re-election should also be re-elected together in this election. However, this matter concerns the election policy, and careful examination is necessary to seek details. For the sake of prudence, we have prepared a document and submitted it to your bureau for review and approval. This is for the public convenience."

International Telegraph Administration

Ordered to Strictly Prohibit Telegraph Operators from Holding Concurrent Jobs 171

The Ministry of Communications, after discovering that some telegraph personnel were holding concurrent jobs in privately-run radio stations and setting up private transceivers to seek personal gain, specially instructed the International Telegraph Administration to stop this practice. After receiving the order, the Administration immediately issued a notice stating: "It has long been prohibited for the administration's reporting staff to hold concurrent jobs in privately-run radio stations. However, as time passes, the rules have been violated. According to confidential reports, there are still a few telegraph operators holding concurrent jobs outside and setting up private transceivers to seek personal gain. They are given one week to voluntarily resign from their concurrent jobs. Otherwise, they will be dismissed and punished as soon as they are discovered. However, those who can accurately report the names of the above-mentioned people holding concurrent jobs will be rewarded with cash. If someone makes a false accusation out of spite, they will be severely punished upon verification and will not be spared. This is the notice."

Wing On Cotton Mill

Payment of Relief Funds to Laid-Off Workers: Collection on May 15th 172

The Wing On Second Cotton Mill in Wu Song, located west of Yunzaobang, experienced a riot in December 1931 due to a labor-management dispute, which resulted in the factory being destroyed by the crowd and a female worker, Jiao Lianying, being injured and dying. The police department arrested eleven workers who led the trouble and sent them to the court, where they were sentenced to imprisonment. Except for Shen Shegen, Pan Zhenquan, and Xu Hengdi, who died of illness while in custody, the remaining eight people, including Shen Yongming and Jin Yaowen, were only released last year after serving their terms. The factory was approved by the municipal government to pay relief funds of 2,000 yuan to the laid-off workers and has submitted the funds to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs. The bureau issued a notice yesterday, instructing the workers to go to collect the funds. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Notice No. 2050 is recorded as follows: "It has been verified that after the resolution of the labor-management dispute at the Wing On Second Cotton Mill, all the relief funds to be paid, amounting to 2,000 yuan, have been submitted to the bureau by the factory. It is now scheduled to be distributed at the Wu Song Doushi Road Fire Brigade from 10:00 AM to 4:00 PM on May 15th. The detailed distribution list is listed below for public knowledge. The laid-off workers of the factory, including Huang Xin Zhou, should come to collect the funds at that time. This is the notice." The distribution list for the relief funds of 2,000 yuan is as follows: "(1) 123 laid-off workers are listed below. The first 44 were approved to be dismissed by the Municipal Government in January 1932. The remaining 79 were dismissed when the factory resumed operations after the Shanghai Battle of 1932 because new workers had already been hired. Each person should receive 10 yuan, totaling 1,230 yuan (names of the 123 people are omitted). (2) Four deceased people are listed below. The first person was injured and died during the riot in December 1931. The remaining three were the families of those who died of illness while in custody in court. Each should receive 70 yuan, totaling: Jiao Lianying, Shen Fugen, Pan Zhenquan, Xu Hengdi. (3) The remaining 490 yuan will be distributed according to the size of their wages by the eight people listed below who were detained by the court for the riot in December 1931: Shen Yongming, Jin Yaowen, Shen Yuelin, Zhang Zhenquan, Shen Yongqing, Zhu Biao, Lei Youqing, Li Asan. May 1st, Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs, Wu Xingya."

Tenant Representatives of Peide Lane

Negotiated with the Water Company Again Yesterday: No Results After Several Hours of Negotiations 173

Since the water was cut off in Peide Lane on Xin Zha Road, despite efforts to appeal to various parties, the water source has not been restored due to the insistence of the owner and the water company. Wang Xiangu, the lawyer representing the lane, received a reply letter from the water company yesterday that misinterpreted the sentences. He immediately sent another letter in reply and accompanied the tenant representatives to negotiate with the water company. The details are recorded below.

Not Allowed to Turn on the Water 174

Yesterday afternoon, Wang Xiangu, the lawyer representing the lane, accompanied representatives Liu Chengyong, Chen Silong, Pan Sanquan, and three others to negotiate with the British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company. The deputy manager, a Westerner named Walder, met them. Wang Xiangu translated the purpose of the visit, requesting the company to immediately send someone to turn on the water, and the water fee would be paid by the tenant representatives to avoid losses to the company. However, according to Walder, he was not allowed to turn on the water and could only do so if separate water meters were installed. However, the tenant representatives firmly refused to install separate meters until the water fees paid by the owner in the rent were refunded. After several hours of negotiations, there were still no results. Finally, the representatives stated that if the company did not fulfill its obligations under the treaty and did not turn on the water, the company would be fully responsible for any accidents that occurred as a result. The meeting ended unhappily.

Company Reply Letter 175

The British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company replied to the representing lawyer, Wang Xiangu, yesterday, stating: "In reply, we received your lawyer's letter on the 27th of this month, stating that you are providing water to the houses on Xin Zha Road and Da Tong Road, Tianzhutang. We understand. It has been verified that the owner of each house has accepted the conditions for installing separate meters in that location. He has requested our company to install the separate meters in accordance with the patent contract. Since the entire chapter has been accepted, the company should implement the installation of the separate meters in accordance with the terms of the patent contract with the Shanghai Municipal Council. The terms of the contract cited by your lawyer are not relevant to this matter, because the owner has accepted the various terms of the contract, so after the implementation, the owner has no responsibility for paying the fees. Even if the owner still has this responsibility, the company is free to stop supplying water, because the sentence in that clause states, 'It has not been determined whether the company can stop supplying water at the request of the landlord.' In view of the above situation, your lawyer can know that if the company continues to supply water, it will not be able to collect water fees from the landlord or the tenants. Therefore, after the failure of reconciliation, the supply will be stopped. However, in the opinion of the company, there is no reason why the installation of separate water meters is detrimental to the tenants. If the situation still wants to be discussed in detail, please ask your lawyer to inform the situation to come to our company to discuss everything in person. This is for lawyer Wang Xiangu. Secretary and Deputy Manager, Walder, opened."

Re: Letter to the Water Company 176

Yesterday, the neighborhood again sent a letter to the Water Company, stating:

To whom it may concern:

We have received your esteemed letter and immediately forwarded it to all tenants of Peide Lane, Xinzha Road, for their review. According to their response, the water supply for the tenants should be continued by the Water Company. This is clearly stated in the contract clauses between your company and the Public Works Department on March 17, 1928, specifically, "If the house is occupied, the Water Company shall not, at the request of the landlord, discontinue the water supply." It is difficult to accept your company's attempts to shirk responsibility. Moreover, your company previously sent a letter to a certain organization with real estate interests, based on the same contract, automatically declaring that if a house is occupied by tenants, the Water Company shall not comply with the landlord's request to cut off the water supply to all or part of the house, and that the outstanding water charges can be recovered from the landlord using the landlord's property as collateral. This shows that the Water Company was well aware of its obligation to supply water to the tenants and should strictly and consistently adhere to it, making it impossible to violate or undermine. In your reply, the Water Company quoted the phrase in the aforementioned contract clause, "Whether or not the company can stop at the request of the landlord is not fixed," (the original wording is actually that the Water Company shall not comply with the landlord's request to cut off the water supply), and should pay attention to the phrase "the house is occupied." It should be understood that the water supply is a public utility. For the sake of protecting public interests, it should be restricted by the municipal government through laws and regulations and should not abuse freedom to harm the lives of the public. As for the statement that the owner has already accepted the contract (the original letter did not specify which contract), and that there is no responsibility for the payment of fees, it is not worth considering. It must be understood that private contracts that violate laws and regulations and harm public interests are invalid. Your company is one of the large companies exclusively engaged in public utilities, and how could you not know this principle and deliberately make excuses? The tenants believe that the Water Company's cutting off the water supply to Peide Lane is a small matter, but undermining the exclusive contract is a big matter. Undermining the exclusive contract means that the company loses its basis for existence. The tenants also firmly believe that the Water Company has an absolute and strict obligation to abide by the exclusive contract, and that supplying water to tenants and collecting water charges from landlords is legally sound. However, reading the last paragraph of your company's reply, stating that it is difficult to collect water charges from the owner or tenants if the water supply is continued, suggests that your company has difficulties in collecting fees from the owners. The tenants may, in fact, be willing to pay on their behalf and are willing to provide a cash guarantee, so there is no reason for the company to cut off the water supply again. As the water supply has been cut off for ten days, there is no time to wait. We hereby request that the company restore the water supply within 24 hours of receiving this letter, and ensure that such inhuman behavior does not occur again in the future. If the company remains stubborn, stubbornly refuses to supply water, and unreasonably oppresses us, it will inevitably put more than 3,000 tenants to death, which is tantamount to re-enacting the May 30th tragedy today. Therefore, in order to safeguard the exclusive contract, save our own lives, and protect the interests of all residents in the concession, the tenants, in addition to publicizing the facts to the world, will have no choice but to take necessary measures to deal with everything in response to the emergency and danger. Your company shall be responsible for the unfortunate consequences arising therefrom. We respectfully request you to forward this letter and hope that you will give it serious consideration. This letter is addressed to the British Shanghai Water Company.

Resolution of Water Dispute 180

The tenants of Shishan Lane on Dongxi Huade Road in Hongkou were repeatedly notified by the Water Company to sign contracts with the company and pay a deposit, otherwise the water would be cut off, causing panic among all the tenants. Regulations for Hospitals Requesting Subsidies to be Observed, Proposed by the Public Works Department and Approved by the Board of Directors 182

The Board of Directors of the Public Works Department has previously decided that all hospitals requesting subsidies and exemptions from donations should first submit reports from the relevant departments for review. It is reported that the Health Department, together with the Public Works Department and the Fire Department, has drafted several regulations to be observed by the hospitals. It has been submitted to the Health Committee for detailed review and was approved by the Board of Directors yesterday. The proposed principles are listed below: (A) Regarding staff: 1. Each hospital should have a sufficient number of physicians to cope with outpatients and inpatients. The physicians must be registered with the Public Works Department. 2. In addition to assistants and trainee nurses, the hospital should have a sufficient number of graduate nurses, at least one. 3. The hospital pharmacy is best managed by a qualified pharmacist. All poisons may only be used by physicians and trained nurses or pharmacists and must be kept locked at all times. Hospitals with 50 or more beds and requesting subsidies must have one trained pharmacist. (B) Regarding construction: 1. The light and air in the wards must be sufficient (each bed should get 800 cubic feet of air, and there should be a window between every two beds). There should be someone to attend to each large room. Patients must have individual beds, mattresses, and clothing. The hospital should prepare ordinary indoor supplies. 2. The operating room must be well-lit and easy to clean. All those accepting major surgical and obstetric cases should have such a room. 3. The hospital should have equipment for emergency first aid for injuries. 4. Nurses must have clean living rooms and bathing facilities. Those on night duty are best provided with separate living quarters. 5. Servants' rooms must have clean and bathing facilities. 6. The kitchen should be set up in accordance with the conditions of the Health Department. 7. Toilets must be numerous and isolated from flies. The disposal of filth must have appropriate measures. 8. Infectious excrement and bandages must be incinerated or disinfected before disposal. 9. Regarding death and mourning, there should be equipment that is satisfactory to the Health Department. (C) Other conditions: 1. Each floor of the hospital must have a sufficient supply of clean water. 2. Furniture, equipment, and decoration must be fully functional. 3. Each patient, whether outpatient or inpatient, must register their condition, treatment, medication, and address. 4. The general cleanliness and management of the hospital must comply with the standards of the Health Department. Rules to be observed by hospitals requesting subsidies: 1. The names and addresses of the hospital director, physicians, and chief stewards must be reported in detail to the Public Works Department. Any changes must be reported immediately. 2. Construction situation. Hospital construction should be maintained in good condition. No modifications or additions may be made without the prior permission of the Public Works Department. 3. Fire insurance and prevention. (A) The fire extinguishers installed in accordance with the bureau's regulations should be maintained at all times so that they can be used. (B) The safety equipment prepared for patients and staff should be maintained in accordance with the regulations. All exit doors must be marked and open outwards. (C) All electrical installations must comply with the bureau's regulations. The location of the main switch room or the main switch must be permitted first and clearly marked. (D) The storage location of all X-ray films and pharmaceutical test products shall be handled in accordance with the instructions of the bureau. 4. Infectious diseases. Those who have been identified as smallpox, diphtheria, nuclear plague, scarlet fever, or cerebrospinal inflammation shall not be admitted. As for other infectious diseases, if the hospital has sufficient isolation and nursing equipment, and the bureau's isolation hospital has no vacancies, they may also be admitted. Hospitals specifically licensed by the Health Department may admit cholera and similar summer diseases. 5. Report of infection. Whenever a hospital discovers an infectious disease, whether outpatient or inpatient, it shall immediately report it to the Health Department in the prescribed format. When patients with infectious diseases are discharged from the hospital, the disinfection measures shall be handled in accordance with the regulations of the Health Department. 6. Statistics of life and death. Births and deaths in hospitals shall be reported to the Health Department in the prescribed format. 7. Legal events. If the hospital finds the following circumstances: (A) Gunshot wounds. (B) Injuries caused by similar blunt or sharp objects. (C) Poisoning. (D) Injuries caused by accidents (including industrial accidents), it shall immediately report to the Police Department by telephone and then submit a written report in the prescribed format. In addition to the above, all unnatural deaths must be reported as above. The corpse may not be removed without the permission of the Police Department. 8. Annual report. The hospital shall prepare a statistical report every year. All records shall be submitted immediately when requested. 9. Bureau staff inspection. Representatives dispatched by the Public Works Department may enter the hospital for inspection at all appropriate times. 10. Stop illegal rules. The hospital shall not give any fees to any staff of the Public Works Department.

Minutes of the Executive Board Meeting of the Road Association 183

The China National Road Construction Association held its tenth executive board meeting yesterday. The executive directors present were Wang Zhengting, Zhu Shaoping (represented by Zhu Hongjun), Wu Shan, Fan Guang, Li Zhaohuan, Yin Ruli, Li Denghui, and Wu Kaisheng. Wang Zhengting chaired the meeting, and Jiang Rongsheng took the minutes. The matters resolved are as follows: (A) Report matters: (1) The appointment of Wang Shaoji as a special commissioner to inspect road and municipal administration in Japan is requested for retroactive recognition. Resolution: Retroactive recognition is approved. (2) Registration rules for specialized talents in the service department are requested for retroactive recognition. Resolution: The original title "China National Road Construction Association Service Department Registration Rules for Civil, Mechanical, Automotive Engineering, Railway, Automobile Management and Accounting Specialized Talents" should add the word "Road" in the middle of Railway and Automobile. Also, in Article 3, add "together with supporting documents, send to this department. After registration, the supporting documents will be sent back to the individual." The original Article 5 should be canceled immediately, and Article 6 should be changed to Article 5, and so on. Also, in item 5 of the registration form, the word "what" in "what subject studied" should be changed to the word "specialty". All others are passed. (B) Discussion matters: (1) The Secretary-General drafted a general report on the work of the association, please review it, and ask Vice President Li to send someone to translate it into German and send it to Minister Liu to be taken to the International Road Conference for distribution. Executive Director Li Yaosheng suggested that the chairman should appoint an executive director to review the text. The chairman then appointed Li Yaosheng and Fan Zhenchu to review and translate it. (2) Member Jiang Hong wrote to request to represent the association at the International Road Conference and wrote to request the committee to subsidize travel expenses. Resolution: Handled by the secretariat. (3) The collection of members in the previous session, the outer teams should be urged to inquire about the scheduled end date. Resolution: The deadline is May 31. Urge the teams according to the resolution. If there are membership fees, they must be submitted to the meeting within the time limit for reporting. Letters are sent out twice, on May 1 and May 15. (4) The former collection team leader Xu Genghua owed the association membership fees, and repeated collections were unsuccessful. Can Kunshan stone be used as collateral? Resolution: The membership fees owed by Xu should be recovered to emphasize public funds, and the Kunshan stone should be returned. (5) Plan to publish "Road Architecture" and ask to determine the number of royalties. Resolution: The Secretary-General should consider the cost of printing the book, how much it can be sold, and how to raise the printing costs, and then decide. As for the royalties, it is stipulated that 20% of the sales cost will be allocated. (6) Mao Zongquan, chairman of the Jiangxi branch, wrote to request that the authorities be notified to restore the branch. Resolution: Reply that the association is now planning a new plan for organizing branches, and will handle it after it is drafted. Although the association has regulations on the "Outline of Branch Organization" for the organization of branches in provinces, cities, and counties, there are still many to be deleted and revised. The Secretary-General should draft a plan and submit it to the next board meeting for discussion. (This) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs came to inform us that the German envoy was informed that the time of the Seventh International Road Congress happened to be the 25th anniversary of the establishment of the Standing Joint Association of the International Road Association. Resolution: The association should send a letter of congratulations and reply to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for reference. The meeting adjourned at 7:30.

Architectural Association

Improving Chinese Architecture, Sending Personnel to Beiping to Visit Palaces, Collecting Materials for Research 184

Modern Chinese architecture is tending towards Westernization, losing its inherent artistic characteristics of the East. Moreover, due to the need for imported building materials, the annual outflow of money is countless. The Shanghai Architectural Association, in view of this, is sparing no effort in studying Eastern architectural art. Recently, Du Yigeng, Liu Jiasheng, Peng Bogang, and others were appointed to the architecture, art, construction, and materials groups, respectively, to travel to Beiping to visit the Forbidden City, collect materials, and study them. The magnificent palace-style architecture is combined with economical and practical Western methods to create modern, economical, and useful architectural forms for the architectural community to choose from, in order to preserve China's inherent artistic characteristics and recover the huge financial losses. It is reported that the representatives have scheduled to depart for the north on the 10th of this month and will publish their findings in the Architectural Monthly published by the association.

Page 12

Japanese Sugar Intensifies Production

Preparing for Large-Scale Exports to China for Dumping, Domestic Sugar Sales Showing Signs of Improvement, But the Overall Future of the Sugar Market Remains Pessimistic 190

China's sugar market has long been occupied by Japanese merchants. In recent years, due to the bankruptcy of domestic rural areas and the weak purchasing power of the people, sales have become increasingly narrow, and the future of the sugar industry is quite pessimistic. However, Japanese sugar companies still plan to export large quantities to China for dumping. The reporter of the Dagong Daily investigated the recent situation from all parties yesterday and will record it separately below.

Japanese Sugar Efforts Increase Exports to China 191

It is learned that Japan's sugar

manufacturing industry, due to

the poor export of sugar to

China in recent years, is

actively taking measures to

reduce production and limit

the supply in the country,

storing as much excess sugar

as possible to maintain the

equilibrium of supply and demand. However, recently, the Governor-General of Taiwan suddenly encouraged production in order to restore the exports to China in recent years. This year, it is preparing to increase production by 5.2 million dan, planning to transport half of it to China for dumping in order to occupy the East Asian sugar market.

Sluggish Sales Lead to Import Reduction 192

In recent days, the sales volume of sugar in this city has sharply decreased due to increased import tariffs, financial difficulties, and weak purchasing power. In previous years, the total monthly imports often exceeded 300,000 dan. However, recently, it has been only around 30,000 dan, less than one-tenth of the previous amount. The stock in warehouses, at its peak, once exceeded one million dan. However, the total sugar stock in March of this year has been reduced again, to just over 180,000 dan. Judging by its origin, it includes 85,000 dan of Java sugar, 65,000 dan of Cuban sugar, 12,000 dan of Hong Kong sugar, and 10,000 dan each of Shantou and Japanese sugar.

Domestic Refined Sugar Gradually Shows Improvement 193

According to sources in the sugar industry, the quantity of domestic sugar produced in Guangdong's Chaozhou and other places and shipped to Shanghai has been increasing daily. Each sailing vessel imports around 500 to 600 dan of domestic sugar, with a total monthly import of about 10,000 dan. The market price is only 12 to 16 yuan per dan. Although its quality is equivalent to brown sugar or raw sugar, its sales are quite strong due to its low market price. The sales of general foreign sugar have been greatly affected as a result.

Sugar Prices Plunge, Future Pessimistic 194

According to an investigation by a reporter from the Ta Kung Pao, there are currently more than sixty sugar merchants (wholesale outlets) in Shanghai. Last year, due to exchange rate fluctuations, the market price of sugar plummeted, causing significant losses to various businesses. Among them, three or four companies declared bankruptcy due to excessive losses. The remaining businesses have also suffered considerable blows. According to some estimates, even more sugar businesses may close down during the May settlement period this year. The future of the sugar trade remains extremely pessimistic.

Huangpu Conservancy Bureau Announcement

High Tide to Occur in the City, Height Reaching 11.45 Feet, Starting from 1:20 AM on the 30th 195

According to the Datong News Agency, the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau announced its tidal forecast for this month yesterday. A reporter from the Datong News Agency learned from the bureau yesterday that a high tide will occur from 1:20 AM to 4:12 AM on the 30th of this month, with an estimated maximum height of 11.45 feet. The speed of the water flow will be 2.2 nautical miles per hour (one nautical mile per hour is 6080 feet, or 0.515 meters per second). The tide will be slightly lower during the same period on the 31st, with an estimated height of 11.00 feet, and the speed of the water flow will also be 2.2 nautical miles per hour.

Three Germans in a Small Boat

Travel Across the Ocean to Shanghai, One Gave Up Mid-Journey Due to Weakness, Two Arrived Safely in Shanghai Yesterday 196

According to the Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury, Germans Knecht and Teus, both under the age of thirty, along with another person, left Germany in an unsinkable boat three years ago. They sailed along the Mediterranean Sea for six months, then headed east, passed through the Suez Canal, and reached India. Continuing to Calcutta, they sold the boat and bought a larger wooden lifeboat. The new boat was 27 feet long and 27 feet wide. They crossed the Bay of Bengal and reached Yangon. Because the boat was small, they could not sleep comfortably and often stayed on the waterfront at night. The other person gave up mid-journey due to weakness. Upon reaching Burma, the two changed to a more comfortable steamboat, stopping in many places along the way. They arrived in Shanghai last night (the 2nd). The two now intend to find a steamboat capable of crossing the Pacific Ocean and plan to cross the ocean this summer, pass through the Panama Canal, and return home. However, the two are unable to afford to purchase one, so they plan to seek assistance from people in Shanghai.

Spring Fish Arrived in Song Yesterday, The Leading Ship is Named Er He Sheng, Loaded with Five Holds of Yellow Croaker 197

The first ship of the annual Northern Yellow Croaker fishing season from Wusong arrived yesterday afternoon. The ship is named Er He Sheng, from Sannan, Shandong. It caught five holds of fish, which were sold through the Bing Feng Fish Company. The holds were opened and sold immediately, and were quickly sold out. According to the fishermen, the fishing season started very early this year. Fish were found as early as the 16th and 17th days of the third month of the lunar calendar, and the fishing season is quite prosperous. Many fishing boats have caught fish, and a large number of fishing boats are expected to arrive in the coming days.

Japanese Yen Soars

Chinese Merchants Continue to Go Bankrupt 198

According to the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun, due to the recent fall in silver prices and the rise in the Japanese yen, Japanese residents are experiencing mixed fortunes due to exchange rate fluctuations. However, speculative Chinese merchants, during this period, have seen both fortunes made and bankruptcies suffered. In the past few days, the rise and fall of the Japanese yen has been erratic (last month, 100 Chinese silver dollars could be exchanged for 116 Japanese yen, but the previous day it suddenly fell to 101 yen). It is reported that the losses of Chinese speculators have reached 30 million yuan, with Cantonese exchange shops suffering the most. The most serious case is Su Heting of Yih Heng Silver Shop on Tianjin Road, who is from Tianjin. He was engaged in this business and suffered losses of 1.2 to 1.3 million yuan. He suddenly became disgusted with the world and attempted suicide by taking opium at the Astor House Hotel. Fortunately, he was discovered early, and his life is not in danger. There are countless others who have failed in speculation.

Explosion of a Bomb in Lan Ni Du

Bean Curd Shop Employee Dies Tragically, Source of Bomb Unknown, Employee's Death Gruesome 199

A bomb suddenly exploded in the bean curd shop opened by Sha Sanyuan, a local, at No. 133 Huayuan Stone Bridge Street in Lan Ni Du, Pudong, at 1:00 AM yesterday morning. The loud bang shook the surrounding area, and nearby residents were awakened from their dreams and rushed out to investigate. They saw smoke billowing from the entrance of the shop, with a strong smell of sulfur. Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the Third District of the Public Security Bureau, rushed to the scene to investigate after being notified by the police. He saw Chen Shiying, an employee of the shop, lying on the ground, his head wounded by the explosion, his face covered in blood, and his right eyeball protruding, groaning in agony. He immediately ordered him to be taken to the Pudong Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he was transferred to the Shanghai Medical College Hospital that night for treatment. Chen's brain was severely concussed, and he bled from all seven orifices. He died of his injuries at 7:00 AM in the morning. The hospital notified the court to conduct an autopsy by telephone. In order to understand the origin of the bomb, District Chief Zhang sent household registration inspector Cao Hongci to investigate in detail yesterday morning. According to the shop owner Sha Sanyuan, he has been running the bean curd shop at that location for seven or eight years and has no enemies. Chen Shiying, the shop employee, was 27 years old and from Gujia Roadkou in Pudong. He had been an apprentice in the shop since he was a child and was quite diligent and thrifty. He got up at midnight every night to work. He was raking out the ashes from the stove and pouring them beside the water tank at 1:00 AM that night (i.e., early on the 3rd) when a bomb suddenly exploded in the corner of the wall, killing him. He did not know where it came from. Inspector Cao recovered several pieces of the shattered bomb casing at the scene, each about two-tenths of an inch thick, and took them back to the bureau for examination. Chen Shiying, the shop employee who was tragically killed, was the only son, 27 years old this year, and had just married last year. His father died early, and he only had a mother at home.

Robbers Disguised as Rickshaw Pullers

Detectives Intercept and Arrest on the Way, One Pulling a Rickshaw, One Riding a Bicycle, One Walking, Two Handguns and Many Bullets Found in the Vehicles - Previously Committed Major Robbery and Murder Case - 200

Jin Jiulin, the inspector general of the special agency of the French Concession police, received a secret report on the afternoon of the day before yesterday that robbers disguised as rickshaw pullers and bicycle riders were going to rob on Haig Road and would pass through the intersection of Ba Xian Qiao, Route Ma Gao Bao Lu, and Route Wagner. Inspector General Jin then led detectives Zhang Ziying and Qian Yumin, deputy detective Zhou Bingcheng, and detectives Liu Dianlong, Cai Jinzhang, and Ma Yizhi to the above-mentioned location, where they lay in ambush. At 4:30 PM, they saw three people, one riding a bicycle, one pulling a rickshaw, and one walking alongside, coming from east to west. Their appearance was suspicious. The detectives rushed forward, surrounded the three, and inspected the bicycle, which was numbered 19869, and the rickshaw license, which was numbered 1712. They found two Browning handguns, numbered 554 and 26580, and thirteen bullets in the gun case under the rickshaw seat, with two clips loaded with bullets. They immediately took them to the police station for questioning. The bicycle rider gave his name as Zhou Xuan, 27 years old, from Funing. The rickshaw puller gave his name as Hua Si, also known as Yi Ming, 49 years old, from Jiangbei. The pedestrian gave his name as Chen Chunfang, also known as A San, 32 years old, from Jiangbei. The detectives then discovered that the robbery of Xu Zhishan, a Yangzhou resident who ran an old stamp business at No. 31 Jin Yu Li, Route de Pesson, at 7:00 PM on March 26 of this year, and the shooting of Detective Li Qiliang of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau of Zhabei, who was with his partner Li Liangfu, by robbers who opened fire on pedestrians being inspected on Jiaotong Road, resulting in the death of both men, were committed by the same robbers. When questioned, the three robbers confessed without hesitation. They also confessed to committing many robberies in the French Concession. The detectives reported the information to the Western Police Chief, who ordered them to be detained separately. Yesterday at noon, they were escorted to the Second Special District Court, where Judge Li Changnian sat in the first criminal court to hear the case. Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, stated the case, saying that the defendants had committed many robberies and murder cases and that the police had not yet begun investigating due to time constraints. He requested a postponement of two weeks to detain the defendants while the details of the case were investigated and prosecuted. He also presented the handguns and bullets to the court. The court verified the report, briefly questioned the three defendants, and then approved the postponement for further investigation. The defendants were returned to custody.

Guangzhao Shelf Trade

Rende Hall Lawsuit, Li Jiafu Sues Lu Bingjie First, Lu Sues Li for Financial Review - Court Orders Postponement for Ten Days - 201

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs previously received reports accusing the directors of the Rende Hall of the Shanghai Guangzhao Shelf Trade of illegally selling the hall's public property, engaging in fraudulent accounting, and controlling the hall's affairs. Therefore, it ordered the hall to be reorganized and instructed Lu Bingjie, a member of the trade association, to take over all affairs before the reorganization. Subsequently, Lu complied with the order and convened a reorganization meeting on March 19, electing members to the reorganization committee and resolving to dismiss the old directors, including Li Jiafu. At the same time, he requested the First Special District Court to return the hall's deposits at the Commercial Bank that had been submitted to the court. However, Li Jiafu and others believed that the accusations against them were mostly fabricated. In addition to complying with the order to submit the hall's accounts and books to the Bureau of Social Affairs for investigation and making a defense, they specifically hired lawyer Chen Huanyin to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Lu Bingjie, requesting that the resolutions of March 9 be declared invalid. The court had already summoned them once, which was reported in the newspapers. It is now known that Lu Bingjie's side, in response to the lawsuit filed by Li Jiafu, Chen En, and others, has also filed a lawsuit against Li and Chen for financial review through their representative lawyer, in addition to legally defending themselves. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan held a hearing. According to Chen Zhongyin, the lawyer representing Li and others, the hearing was originally for the preservation of evidence requested by the plaintiffs Li Jiafu and others. However, since the case was filed, it had been mediated by the Guangdong fellow villagers, and Li Dachao, the section chief of the Municipal Government, had reached a settlement with both parties. On April 26, Mr. Li sent the draft settlement agreement to both parties, and a formal contract would be signed on April 30. Before the formal contract was signed, he requested that the case be temporarily suspended. He also submitted a copy of the draft agreement to the court. However, Lu's representative lawyer expressed disagreement with the so-called settlement, stating that he had never entrusted Mr. Li to mediate and that Lu Bingjie was now representing 192 members of the trade association in suing Li Jiafu, Chen Enbao, and others, requesting that they hand over all accounts for review. This case was completely different from the lawsuit filed by Li and others and should be investigated. Judge Qiao then ordered the lawyer to state the reasons for the lawsuit. He then stated that the Rende Hall was similar in nature to a trade union and that the hall's property was donated by all members of the trade association and should be owned by all members, not just a few individuals. According to the hall's regulations, all accounts should be publicly reported every month and published in a credit record, and an annual final account should be prepared at the end of the year. However, since June of last year, the accounts had never been published, and no credit record had been issued. The defendants all had duties and should be held responsible. Therefore, he requested that they be ordered to hand over the accounts for review. Lawyer Chen stated that the hall's accounts had already been submitted to the Bureau of Social Affairs and that all members of the hall had the right to review the accounts and could request the Bureau of Social Affairs to review them. However, those who were not members could not request to review the accounts. However, he had only recently learned of Lu Bingjie's lawsuit against Li and others and had not had time to prepare the defense procedures or submit the power of attorney. The court then ordered a postponement until the afternoon of May 10 for further hearing.

Impersonating French Consul to Defraud

Three Russians Convicted 202

Russians Lai Weiqi Ji, Lao Maimo Nuofu, and Bao Baofu were previously arrested for falsely impersonating the French vice consul, French chief patrol, and detective chief to defraud Xu Haidu, a Chinese national, by claiming to be able to issue gambling licenses and requesting 30,000 yuan in expenses. The French Concession Police Western Detective Fan Langdeng discovered this and arrested Lai and the other two, along with persons involved, Si Duinao Fa and La Guliya Fa Ladimier. They collected various evidence and sent them to the Second Special District Court for public prosecution, announcing the end of the trial and awaiting a scheduled sentencing. This was previously reported in the newspaper. Yesterday was the date of the verdict. At 10:00 AM, the police escorted the defendants to the court, where Judge Sun Pengxian presided over the third criminal court, ordering the defendants to be brought to the court. Lai Weiqi Ji and Lao Maimo Nuofu were sentenced to one year of imprisonment each for jointly committing attempted fraud as recidivists. Bao Baofu was sentenced to one month of imprisonment for assisting in attempted fraud. The judgment was final.

The number of days previously detained will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Si Duinao Fa and La Guliya Fa Ladimier were found not guilty. The attached civil suit will be transferred to the civil court for trial.

First Attempted Suicide Saved

Second Hanging Fatal, Cheng Yongnong's Fate Due to Gambling, Last Testament Strongly Condemns the Harms of Gambling 203

Cheng Yongnong, from Anhui, 24 years old, was previously a weaver at the Xie Sheng Electrical Silk Weaving Factory at No. 81 Huade Road. He was addicted to gambling and, recently, was unable to repay his gambling debts. Therefore, not long ago, he became distraught and conceived the idea of ending his life. He rented a room at the Yangzi Hotel and attempted suicide by smoking opium. He was discovered and the Lao Zha Police Station was notified, which ordered detectives to take him to the hospital, where he was saved. However, Cheng's determination to die was unwavering. The day before yesterday, he went to Room 7 of the Dalu Hotel at No. 640 Lane 6, Huade Road, alone and hanged himself. When the tea boy Zhao Huatang discovered him, he immediately tried to untie him, but he was already in critical condition. He immediately reported to the Yulin Road Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. They then took him to St. Luke's Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died. A suicide note was found next to him, in which he described the harms of gambling and his inability to survive, which led him to have suicidal thoughts. The detectives then took his body to the Fielun Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Diao Chengtang, accompanied by forensic clerk Wang Zuyi, to the morgue to examine the body. According to Cheng Songyi, 29 years old, the deceased was his nephew, and his father was currently in their hometown. He was not aware of his actions until someone told him. He was now taking the body on behalf of his family. According to Zhao Huatang's statement, Mr. Diao issued a verdict that the deceased, Cheng Yongnong, had indeed died by hanging himself and ordered that the body be handed over to Cheng Songyi to be taken back for burial after he signed a guarantee.

Setting up Stalls at the Jing'an Temple Fair Will Not Disrupt Store Business 204

There are many stalls at the Jing'an Temple Bathing Buddha Festival every year. This year, the shops in the area near the temple sent a letter to the Public Works Department with their concerns. Yesterday, the Director-General of the Public Works Department replied, saying that they would try to reduce the impact of the temple fair on shop traffic. The number of stalls will be less than in previous years, and there will be space behind the stalls and in front of the shops to allow convenient access for all shops. The Public Works Department has also announced that, for this year's and future temple fairs, stallholders are only allowed to sell Chinese handicrafts.

Public Works Department Does Not Approve Reduction of Bicycle Tax 205

The Public Works Department of the International Settlement, following a proposal by the French Concession, decided to increase the annual bicycle tax from three yuan to four yuan, effective January 1 of next year, and to collect a magnetic license fee of approximately two jiao from April 1 of this year. The Bicycle Manufacturers Association raised objections to this matter, and the Public Works Department reconsidered. After carefully considering the points raised by the association, such as the economic situation of bicycle riders, a comparison of the tax rates in other countries, and the impact on the industry, they concluded that the request could not be approved. The Public Works Department has already replied to the Chinese Ratepayers Association on this matter.

By Feng Youzhen

A Record of Inspection in Xinjiang Published, Distributed by World Book Company 213

The book A Record of Inspection in Xinjiang, written by Feng Youzhen, the secretary of the Ministry of Judicial Administration who accompanied Luo Wengan to Xinjiang last year, was published in newspapers across the country and caused a sensation, attracting attention to the Xinjiang issue. Mr. Feng has now revised the entire book and attached dozens of photographs. The World Book Company has published a separate edition, which has already been released. The entire book contains 100,000 words and provides a very detailed description of the history, geography, customs, and people of Xinjiang, as well as the causes and consequences of the Xinjiang Incident. At a time when the situation on the border is becoming increasingly critical, anyone concerned about border issues should read it. It is said that a Japanese translation of this book has already been made, which shows its value.

Public Works Department Fire Brigade

Recruiting Chinese Trainees 214

The Public Works Department Fire Brigade of the International Settlement currently has several vacancies for Chinese trainees (Cadets). Qualified Chinese citizens are being recruited to fill the positions. Applicants must be between 21 and 25 years old, be physically strong, unmarried, have a certain level of education, be able to read and write English and Chinese official documents, and be able to speak Shanghai dialect and Mandarin. Applicants must first undergo a rigorous physical examination and then be tested on Chinese language and general knowledge. Applicants must submit a written application, written in English, along with supporting documents and a recent photograph, to the Chief Officer, Fire Brigade, S.M.C., No. 309 Henan Road, before Monday, May 21. Applicants may not request an interview, but may send a letter to the Fire Brigade to inquire if they have any questions. Trainees who pass the examination and complete the training period with satisfactory results may be promoted to Sub-Officer in the future.

Summary of Spring Relief in Shaanxi 215

The China Relief Society previously co-sponsored winter relief grain distribution with the Chang'an Branch of Shaanxi, as previously reported. The Society has now sent a letter to the Branch, reporting on the conclusion of the winter relief effort. According to the Branch, the disaster in Shaanxi Province has already reached an unmanageable stage. Now, during the time when there is no new harvest and the old harvest has been depleted, countless people are selling their wives and children, and entire families are dying of starvation or committing suicide. The Branch is heartbroken by this tragic situation and is making efforts to save money and reduce expenses, and is also appealing for donations, while in the process of handling spring relief grain distribution. However, Shaanxi has suffered from years of disasters, it is an extremely poor place, and is unable to assist. The amount of donations collected is very small. It is hoped that charities at home and abroad, when those in distress are awaiting rescue and life is hanging by a thread, can give a donation of one yuan, which can save the life of one more person. Dispatching Personnel to Organize Silver Ear Fungus Farms 216

Szechuan Store at the Ball Game Field in this city, specializing in selling genuine Szechuan silver ear fungus, all Szechuan native products, and ginseng, deer antler, and other precious tonics, has a history of many years. The goods are authentic, and the prices are fair, enjoying a reputation at home and abroad. Even though the market is sluggish, the store's business has been steadily progressing. Recently, it has opened a new main store on the most prosperous Nanjing Road (at the entrance of Pintang Lane) in this city. Due to its long-standing reputation, business is also extremely prosperous. The owner of the store originally owned many silver ear fungus farms in his native Szechuan. The silver ear fungus sold is harvested from his own farms. However, in early last year, after the personnel stationed in the mountains packed and shipped all the silver ear fungus harvested in the summer and autumn seasons, the red bandits occupied areas such as Suiwan, where the silver ear fungus was produced, and were in the hands of the bandits for several months. Now that these places have been recovered by our army, the Szechuan Store specially dispatched personnel who were originally stationed in the mountains a month ago, and hired many skilled personnel familiar with the quality of silver ear fungus producing areas and proficient in baking techniques, to rush to the silver ear fungus farms to actively organize and add huge tree branches for growing ear fungus. The store also, based on the standard of previous scientific testing of the best ear fungus produced in a certain place, re-expanded dozens of silver ear fungus farms to further increase the production of silver ear fungus. The tonic quality of silver ear fungus, and the special effects of treating diseases, are even more abundant. The price paid by people from all walks of life who regularly consume the store's silver ear fungus can also be gradually reduced, and they can also eat better silver ear fungus. It is truly rare to find a business operator in recent times who is as considerate of the interests of customers as the Szechuan Store.

Austrian Commits Suicide with a Handgun 219

In a Western-style apartment at No. 70 Renji Road, lived an Austrian named Faber, 33 years old. The day before yesterday, for unknown reasons, he suddenly committed suicide with a gun. Yao Bingquan, a servant in the apartment, noticed it and immediately reported it to the General Police Station. Western Detective Wick was dispatched to investigate. The man was found lying in the room, his clothes stained with blood. A handgun was next to him. The wound was in his chest. A suicide note was also found, with only a few words, translated as: "My sudden departure from the world is out of necessity. Please inform the consulate immediately to collect my body." The detective took the body to the forensic laboratory on Ferrer Road and took the handgun and other items back to the police station. It was found that the handgun was his own and he had a license. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Diao Chengtang was dispatched by the First Special District Court to examine the body and announced: "The deceased, an Austrian named Faber, was indeed killed by a gunshot wound to the chest. The body is handed over to the Austrian Consulate for burial."

Yuan Hanyun's Lawyer's Residence

Four More Members of Robbery Gang Apprehended - Plotting to Rob Elsewhere - Police Received Information and Arrested Them 221

Yuan Hanyun's, the lawyer, residence at No. 276 Xixiang Lane, Da Tong Road, was broken into on March 10th at 4:30 p.m., and jewelry and silver dollars worth 1,768 yuan were robbed. The Huishi Police Station arrested two robbers, Xu Buzhan, a local, and Chen Yunsheng, from Tongzhou, and sent them to the First Special District Court. Xu was sentenced to ten years and six months of imprisonment, and Chen was sentenced to seven years. The day before yesterday, Wang Guangqi, Hu Guangqi, and Wang Runcheng, Chinese detectives from the Hongkou Police Station, learned that Wang Amao, from Haimen, a member of the robbery gang in this case, along with Chen Guanghao (also known as Cai Ahao) from Yangzhou, and Wang Arong from Haimen, were gathering and discussing in a small teahouse on Avenue Edward VII near Wenzhou Road, plotting to rob a rent collection office near the small bridge on Huade Road. They reported to the police chief and, in cooperation with Western detectives, secretly waited at the location at around 4 p.m. After a while, Wang and the other three arrived. They were arrested. Under interrogation, it was learned that Chen Guanghao had been the informant in the Yuan family robbery, because his wife, Zhang, was working as a servant at Yuan's residence and knew about the money and valuables. The detectives went to No. 191 Zilai Street in the French Concession and arrested Zhang as well. They were all taken to the police station separately for detention. Yesterday morning, Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the Engineering Bureau of the Criminal Division III Court, stated that the defendant Wang Amao was identified by Xu Buzhan, a convicted offender in the settled case, as having participated in the robbery. He had admitted it and even accompanied the detectives to the scene of the crime to demonstrate. Chen Guanghao and Wang Arong admitted that yesterday Wang, who is still at large, and others invited them. The victims and the two criminals, Xu and Chen, were all present in court, but Chen Zhang denied being the informant. This case is requested to be adjourned for detailed investigation. When questioned, the defendants' statements were evasive. According to the victims Yuan Hanyun and his wife, Lin, who testified to the events, and the two criminals, Xu and Chen, who testified that Wang and Wang Amao went to the robbery together, Chen Guanghao and Wang Arong did not go, etc., Judge Wu Zehan ordered the four defendants, including Wang Amao, to be detained separately for further investigation.

Dog Owners Must Obtain Licenses - Dogs Without Muzzles Will Be Captured or Killed 222

The Public Works Department announced that all dog owners who have not yet obtained licenses for this year must apply to the Donation Department or the two police stations on Yangshupu Road and Gordon Road immediately. The fee is five yuan per dog. Clause 4 of the license regulations stipulates that "All dogs on the streets or in public places must be fitted with an effective muzzle, but it must not impede their breathing and drinking." If any dog without a muzzle is found on the roads inside or outside the concession, whether or not it is led by someone, it will be captured by the patrol police and detained in the dog pound for one week or a corresponding period. After the dog owner is identified, he will be prosecuted. A dog's muzzle that is ineffective is also considered as having no muzzle. Any dog without a muzzle that cannot be captured may be shot dead. Those who have lost their dogs and wish to inquire can contact the Gordon Road Police Station (telephone 30015) and the Yangshupu Police Station (telephone 50743).

Small Fire on Guangxi Road 223

The Small Flower Queen Shoe Store on Guangxi Road caught fire at 9:50 p.m. yesterday. The fire suddenly broke out in the storage area upstairs. The Central Fire Brigade dispatched vehicles to put out the fire. By 10:17 p.m., the fire was completely extinguished. Only one room on the upper floor was burned.

French Tram

Dispute Over Ticket Seller Insulting Passengers 224

On a certain No. 2 tram of the French Concession running from the Bund to Xujiahui, at around 8 p.m. on the 1st of this month, while passing the Eight Immortals Bridge from east to west, a dispute arose between the ticket seller No. 210 in the third-class carriage and two passengers over the purchase of tickets due to overcrowding. This is a common occurrence on this tram. However, the ticket seller loudly insulted them, saying that the people who ride the tram are all "low-class people" and "cheapskates." As a result, the passengers in the carriage were in an uproar. Passengers who did not consider themselves "low-class people" or "cheapskates" questioned him, thinking that the passengers are the source of income for ticket sellers, so why should they be regarded as "low-class people" and "cheapskates"? But this ticket seller No. 210 was unreasonable and did not admit his mistake, so he became the target of public criticism. The passengers quarreled and almost came to blows. Seeing that he had angered the public and the situation was unfavorable, the ticket seller quickly ordered the tram to stop and reported to the police. The police mediated and calmed the situation.

French Police Lost Tram Pass Voided 225

Sun Qingshan, a judicial police officer of the First Special District Court of Shanghai, lost his police chief's Tram Company pass No. 711, a small square crystal private seal, and a gold watch while bathing at the Changdechi Bathhouse on Maigen Road at 6 p.m. on the 29th of last month. He specially reported to his superiors to void the pass and issue a new one. The crystal seal was also voided.

Report on Reserves Issued by the Four Banks Reserve Depository - No. 226 226

The Four Banks Reserve Depository is jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks and specializes in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the depository's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves. Cash reserves must be at least 60%, and guarantee reserves must be at most 40%. An announcement is made once a week and is audited by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 226th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Depository on May 1, 23rd year of the Republic of China, is recorded as follows: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 23,548,587 yuan.

Total reserves: 23,548,587 yuan, including cash reserves of 18,984,987 yuan and guarantee reserves of 4,563,600 yuan.

After the association's investigation confirmed this, it unanimously decided to expel him from membership.

Publication of Practical Bank Bookkeeping This book lists the accounting subjects, vouchers, and account forms of banks, as well as their formats. Calligraphy and Painting News 231

Famous Painter Ms. Sun Qionghua Goes to Beijing to Open a Personal Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition Ms. Sun Qionghua is a native of Zhejiang. She is the daughter of Xiaogong and the niece of the Qing historian. She started painting at a young age and obtained natural talent. She studied with Mr. Feng Chaoran, a famous painter in Shanghai, for more than ten years and became famous. After marrying Mr. Sheng Zujiang of Qingyi, she still did not slack off in painting. She once traveled with her husband to Guanwai, where she enjoyed the famous mountains and rivers, and her artistic skills were further advanced. After her husband took office at the Beijing Wireless Telegraph Bureau, comrades in Beijing repeatedly asked her to hold a calligraphy and painting exhibition to feast the eyes of the people in Beijing. It is said that the lady has nodded in agreement and is scheduled to bring more than 70 of her best works, including landscapes, flowers, birds, figures, and ladies, to be displayed at the Central Hotel on May 12th for people to visit. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Movies 233

Jincheng Screens "The Shower of Pear Blossoms" The Jincheng Grand Theater at the intersection of Beijing Road and Guizhou Road not only has sound, light, and seating all of the highest quality, but since its opening, it has repeatedly screened famous and expensive films to please the people of Shanghai. The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that in Northeast China and Shandong, the sky is sunny, with winds from south to west, which are quite strong and sharp. In the Yangtze River basin and the area below, the sky is cloudy, with rain or fog. The wind comes from southeast to southwest. In the coastal area south of Ma'an Island, the wind comes from southeast to northeast. There is a low-pressure area in southwestern China. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the temperature in this city was a maximum of 62.1 and a minimum of 54.9. On the same day last year, the maximum was 70.2 and the minimum was 45.5.

Reading Questions and Answers 238

"A History of the New Chinese Literature Movement"

Questions After Reading Material One

Reading Guidance:

After reading "Historical Materials on the New Chinese Literature Movement" compiled by Huang Ruoying and published by Guangming Bookstore, I cannot help but have the following questions. I am now raising them specifically, and I urge the gentlemen to provide me with a detailed and public answer.

First, what exactly did the "May Fourth Movement" achieve in literature? In this book, from the first to the sixth compilation, almost all are historical materials about the debate between new and old literature before and after the "May Fourth Movement." In these historical materials, we see that the so-called new literature movement at that time was actually a vernacular movement, and all debates started from the point of view of the use of writing. Whether there are defects in this movement itself cannot but make people doubt (because in my opinion, the difference between new and old literature should not only lie in writing), and in its achievements, although Mr. Hu Shi pointed out several key points in the article "Literary Revolution Movement": "First, vernacular poetry can be considered to be on the road to success,... Second, short stories have gradually been established." But I still dare not deeply believe it. If Mr. Hu's so-called "success" refers to changing "zhī hū zhě yě" (classical Chinese particles) to "de me ne ma" (modern Chinese particles), then that's fine, but if not, the success of literary works should also depend on their content, and should also depend on their receptivity to readers. Then I can say that the works created in the May Fourth era that can be given to us to read are really few and far between, except for "Nahan" (Call to Arms) and "Panghuang" (Wandering). For example, Xu Zhimo's poems, no matter how the literary world calls him a "poetry sage", have nothing to do with us. Even if we take a step back and only talk about vernacular Chinese, what they left behind are still some incomprehensible, completely Europeanized sentences, or newly styled classical Chinese that are like restructured bound feet. May I ask, is speech consistent with writing now? Are there many literary publications that the public can understand now?

Second, the fifth compilation of this book is historical material about the issue of sorting out the national heritage. Of course, sorting out the national heritage is not absolutely impossible, because the development of literature is the same as the development of society, and it has its inevitable historical development process. For example, the current Soviet literary world has raised the issue of accepting literary heritage. But I believe that this issue should only be raised when the new literature has already laid its strong foundation. In our country, not long after the May Fourth Movement, the new literature movement cannot be said to have unfolded much. As mentioned above, even the vernacular movement has not completed its initial task. If we turn our heads at this time and delve into a dead end, specializing in what "Dream of the Red Chamber textual research," isn't this obviously picking up the light and neglecting the important, obviously abandoning their current main mission, and obviously rebelling against themselves? Not long ago, someone raised the issue of accepting heritage in a certain issue of literature. May I ask, where is our literary heritage?

Third, there is no doubt that China's new literature movement is still progressing. But what I want to ask is, is the slogan of "restoring the spirit of the May Fourth Movement" correct? What are the similarities between the current literary movement and the May Fourth era? Song Yang's article "The Question of Mass Literature and Art" was published in the previous Literary Monthly, which raised the topic of "what language to write in." He advocated creating a new vernacular Chinese for the masses themselves (not the May Fourth-style vernacular Chinese), but how to create it? Is this inheriting the unfinished vernacular movement in literature of the "May Fourth Movement"?

In addition, there are of course many other questions, such as what role did the Literary Research Association and the early Creation Society play at that time? They are both the main forces of the new literature movement, why did they become opposed to each other? Why did two different literary and artistic trends emerge in the same period—because it is said that the Literary Research Association represented naturalism, while the Creation Society represented romanticism? These are all what we urgently want to know, but if the length is limited, then please answer the three points specifically raised above first.

--Letter from Wang Renkan, Hebei--

Sports News

Amidst Firecrackers, Our National Delegation Departs for the Philippines. Departing at 3:30 PM Yesterday on the McKinley. Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, and Others All Went to the Wharf to See Them Off. 239

The Chinese delegation attending the 10th Far Eastern Games, consisting of over a hundred athletes and staff selected from Shanghai, led by Wang Zhengting, gathered at the new customs wharf yesterday at 2 PM and set off for the Philippines aboard the Dollar Steamship Company's President McKinley. The athletes and staff boarded the ferry in drizzling rain and departed from the new customs wharf at 2 PM, sailing directly to the McKinley at the Bailianjing wharf in Nanshi. The ship set sail at 3:30 PM, with a large crowd of well-wishers. Details are recorded below:

A Glimpse of the Wharf 240

Around 1 PM, the new customs wharf was already crowded with people, because all sectors of society have endless hope that our athletes will bring glory to the country by attending the Far Eastern Games this time. Afterwards, staff and athletes arrived one after another. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Education Bureau Chief Pan Gongzhan, Special Secretary Xiao Tongqian from the Central Propaganda Department, Qian Cangshuo from the Central News Agency, and others all went to the wharf to see them off. The Qin Fen Bookstore also prepared a large flag with the words "Celebrating the Victory of the Chinese Delegation to the Far Eastern Games" and "The Chinese Delegation to the Far Eastern Games Returns Triumphantly with Medals," which had a majestic momentum.

Slowly Leaving the Wharf 241

Those seeing them off were elated, and the delegation members were full of energy. Wang Zhengting, Shen Siliang, Zhou Jiaqi, and others entertained everyone. The ferry left the wharf at 2 PM. For a while, hats and handkerchiefs were waved on the shore and on the ship, expressing extreme emotions of parting. Many of the athletes held cameras and took pictures of those seeing them off as a memento. Workers and police officers from the Sports Association, etc., each donated 60 cents to purchase a large batch of firecrackers to set off at the wharf, adding a lot of color. The relatives and families of the staff and athletes followed the ferry all the way to the large ship.

The Dollar Wharf 242

Sailing through the wind and waves all the way to Nanshi, there was a lot of laughter on the ship, which was very lively. After about three quarters of an hour, they arrived at the edge of the McKinley at the Dollar Wharf in Bailianjing. At that time, firecrackers were also set off at the wharf to welcome them. The Chinese at the Dollar Wharf also prepared a flag that said, "Celebrating the Departure of the Chinese Athlete Delegation to the Philippines," which showed their enthusiasm. The staff and athletes boarded the McKinley one after another, each looking for their reserved room to settle down. At 3:30 PM, the fire was lit and the ship set sail. Everyone stood on the deck to bid farewell to those seeing them off again. The ferry then sailed back to the customs at 3:45 PM.

Arrival Date in the Philippines 243

The funding for this trip to the Philippines is only 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. Fundraising has now ended, but those who continue to donate from various places will be remitted to the Philippines by the Association. Ms. Gao Zi, the head coach of the women's team, was unable to go to the Philippines due to business, and Ma Yuehan also serves as her position. The ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Hong Kong on the afternoon of the 5th to continue loading athletes from Hong Kong and Guangdong. According to the company, it may be delayed until the 6th before arriving in Hong Kong, and arriving in the Philippines should be on the morning of the 8th. It is said that the delegation will take the President Jackson on the 24th of this month to leave the Philippines and return to China, and arrive in Shanghai around the 28th.

Wang Zhengting Speaks 244

Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, Wang Zhengting led the Chinese delegation participating in the Far Eastern Games on the Dollar Steamship Company's McKinley to the Philippines. When Wang boarded the ship at the new customs wharf, he answered reporters' questions and said that rumors that Wang, who also serves as the Minister of Foreign Affairs, would resign and that he would succeed him as Minister of Foreign Affairs, etc., were not known to him. As for going to Jiangxi and Shanxi to meet Chairman Chiang the other day, it was to discuss the Far Eastern Games. The rumors were not true. As for the participation of the puppet state in the Far Eastern Games, it is absolutely not a problem. Our side still holds its original position to seek implementation. According to head coach Ma Yuehan, although our country's hopes are slim in this conference, we have a considerable degree of certainty in scoring in track and field, and our hopes for ball games are even stronger.

Preparing for the Third National Games Next Year

This City Is Building a Great Sports Stadium. An Area of 300 Mu with a Capacity of Over 77,000 People. The Cost is 1 Million Yuan. The Equipment is Extremely Complete and Magnificent. 254

The municipal authorities of this city are actively preparing to build a large sports stadium in this city in order to prepare for the third National Games to be held in Shanghai in October next year. The total cost of the stadium is 1 million yuan, covering an area of more than 300 mu. It has already started bidding and construction, and is scheduled to be completed in August next year. In the future, after completion, it will be the only largest and most complete sports stadium in the Far East. The total capacity of the stadium can accommodate more than 77,300 people. All buildings are planned using the most scientific and latest styles. The reporter made a special note of the details as follows:

The Internal Design is Magnificent The internal design of the large sports stadium 255

Is extremely magnificent, including (1) a track and field venue, including a 500-meter track, two 200-meter tracks, and a football field in the middle, three netball fields, and three basketball fields. (2) Gymnasium, with an internal length of 40 meters and a width of 20 meters, a basketball hoop, a volleyball field, and an indoor netball field. (3) Swimming pool, with a diameter of 50 meters, a width of 20 meters, and depths of 3 feet, 6 feet, and 11 feet in three levels. (4) Netball field, with three hard netball fields. (5) Baseball field, of which the gymnasium also has the latest equipment such as water heaters.

Capacity of Over 70,000 People The internal capacity of the sports stadium built this time 256

Including the track and field venue can accommodate 60,000 people, and a large dormitory is built, which can accommodate more than 3,000 staff and athletes. The gymnasium can accommodate 3,500 people, with 300 lockers. The swimming pool has 4,800 seats, with 340 lockers. The netball field can accommodate 5,000 people, with 100 lockers. The baseball field can accommodate 4,000 people, with 100 lockers. Each field is attached with several shops for selling various items to facilitate spectators and athletes.

Education Subsidies from the Public Works Department 274

A Slight Change in the Principle Regarding Construction Costs

The Education Committee of the Public Works Department previously decided on a principle regarding subsidies for Hua schools, that is, after that, except for urgent needs for cleaning equipment, all construction costs would not be subsidized. The Subsidy Committee subsequently requested that this principle be slightly changed. The Education Committee reviewed it again. Some committee members believed that the previously determined principle was appropriate. Once construction costs are given, the Public Works Department can no longer intervene in the school, unlike the subsidy for annual fees, which can be suspended if there is any non-compliance. Moreover, it is easier for private individuals to raise construction costs, while it is more difficult to donate recurrent expenses. Furthermore, the total amount of subsidies in the bureau is also limited. If everyone asks for help with construction costs, the subsidy for each school's recurrent expenses will be reduced even further. However, according to the Subsidy Committee's vision, it does not advocate giving large sums for construction subsidies. However, in view of the fact that there are very few houses in the concession suitable for schools to rent, it is deemed appropriate for schools to build their own houses and for the Public Works Department to give special consideration and slightly subsidize them to encourage them. After continuous discussion, the Education Committee decided that the previously determined principle did not need to be changed, but if a school builds its own house and can slightly subsidize it to help it succeed, it should be given special consideration.

The Subsidy Committee proposed to give a total of 15,900 yuan in construction subsidies to five schools in 1934, which was approved. In addition, the construction subsidy of 5,600 yuan previously proposed for three schools should be canceled, and this money should be distributed to twelve schools for normal use. This proposal was also approved. In addition, the Subsidy Committee proposed that the subsidies for a certain eight schools should not be reduced (some of which were designated for construction), which was also approved. The construction costs must be used before the end of 1935, and the schools should be notified of this intention. The above points decided by the Education Committee were submitted to the Board of Directors on May 2 and approved.
